<s> Plate--Specimen of Blue China--Indifference to the Laugh of the World--I Discover an Antique En-route to Baden--Baden--Meeting an Old Acquaintance--A young American--Embryo Horse Doctor--An American, Sure--A Minister Captured CHAPTER XXI Baden--Baden--Energetic Girls--A Comprehensive Yawn--A Beggar's Trick--Cool Impudence--The Bath Woman--Insolence of Shop Keepers--Taking a Bath--Early and Late Hours--Popular Belief Regarding Indians--An Old Cemetery--A Pious Hag--Curious Table Companions CHAPTER XV [Charming Waterside Pictures] Men and women and cattle were at work in the dewy fields by this time </s>
<s> The people often stepped aboard the raft, as we glided along the grassy shores, and gossiped with us and with the crew for a hundred yards or so, then stepped ashore again, refreshed by the ride </s>
<s> Only the men did this; the women were too busy </s>
<s> The women do all kinds of work on the continent </s>
<s> They dig, they hoe, they reap, they sow, they bear monstrous burdens on their backs, they shove similar ones long distances on wheelbarrows, they drag the cart when there is no dog or lean cow to drag it--and when there is, they assist the dog or cow </s>
<s> Age is no matter--the older the woman the stronger she is, apparently </s>
<s> On the farm a woman's duties are not defined--she does a little of everything; but in the towns it is different, there she only does certain things, the men do the rest </s>
<s> For instance, a hotel chambermaid has nothing to do but make beds and fires in fifty or sixty rooms, bring towels and candles, and fetch several tons of water up several flights of stairs, a hundred pounds at a time, in prodigious metal pitchers </s>
<s> She does not have to work more than eighteen or twenty hours a day, and she can always get down on her knees and scrub the floors of halls and closets when she is tired and needs a rest </s>
<s> As the morning advanced and the weather grew hot, we took off our outside clothing and sat in a row along the edge of the raft and enjoyed the scenery, with our sun-umbrellas over our heads and our legs dangling in the water </s>
<s> Every now and then we plunged in and had a swim </s>
<s> Every projecting grassy cape had its joyous group of naked children, the boys to themselves and the girls to themselves, the latter usually in care of some motherly dame who sat in the shade of a tree with her knitting </s>
<s> The little boys swam out to us, sometimes, but the little maids stood knee-deep in the water and stopped their splashing and frolicking to inspect the raft with their innocent eyes as it drifted by </s>
<s> Once we turned a corner suddenly and surprised a slender girl of twelve years or upward, just stepping into the water </s>
<s> She had not time to run, but she did what answered just as well; she promptly drew a lithe young willow bough athwart her white body with one hand, and then contemplated us with a simple and untroubled interest </s>
<s> Thus she stood while we glided by </s>
<s> She was a pretty creature, and she and her willow bough made a very pretty picture, and one which could not offend the modesty of the most fastidious spectator </s>
<s> Her white skin had a low bank of fresh green willows for background and effective contrast--for she stood against them--and above and out of them projected the eager faces and white shoulders of two smaller girls </s>
<s> Toward noon we heard the inspiriting cry,-- "Sail ho" </s>
<s> "Where away" </s>
<s> shouted the captain </s>
<s> "Three points off the weather bow" </s>
<s> We ran forward to see the vessel </s>
<s> It proved to be a steamboat--for they had begun to run a steamer up the Neckar, for the first time in May </s>
<s> She was a tug, and one of a very peculiar build and aspect </s>
<s> I had often watched her from the hotel, and wondered how she propelled herself, for apparently she had no propeller or paddles </s>
<s> She came churning along, now, making a deal of noise of one kind or another, and aggravating it every now and then by blowing a hoarse whistle </s>
<s> She had nine keel-boats hitched on behind and following after her in a long, slender rank </s>
<s> We met her in a narrow place, between dikes, and there was hardly room for us both in the cramped passage </s>
<s> As she went grinding and groaning by, we perceived the secret of her moving impulse </s>
<s> She did not drive herself up the river with paddles or propeller, she pulled herself by hauling on a great chain </s>
<s> This chain is laid in the bed of the river and is only fastened at the two ends </s>
<s> It is seventy miles long </s>
<s> It comes in over the boat's bow, passes around a drum, and is payed out astern </s>
<s> She pulls on that chain, and so drags herself up the river or down it </s>
<s> She has neither bow or stern, strictly speaking, for she has a long-bladed rudder on each end and she never turns around </s>
<s> She uses both rudders all the time, and they are powerful enough to enable her to turn to the right or the left and steer around curves, in spite of the strong resistance of the chain </s>
<s> I would not have believed that that impossible thing could be done; but I saw it done, and therefore I know that there is one impossible thing which CAN be done </s>
<s> What miracle will man attempt next </s>
<s> We met many big keel-boats on their way up, using sails, mule power, and profanity--a tedious and laborious business </s>
<s> A wire rope led from the foretopmast to the file of mules on the tow-path a hundred yards ahead, and by dint of much banging and swearing and urging, the detachment of drivers managed to get a speed of two or three miles an hour out of the mules against the stiff current </s>
<s> The Neckar has always been used as a canal, and thus has given employment to a great many men and animals; but now that this steamboat is able, with a small crew and a bushel or so of coal, to take nine keel-boats farther up the river in one hour than thirty men and thirty mules can do it in two, it is believed that the old-fashioned towing industry is on its death-bed </s>
<s> A second steamboat began work in the Neckar three months after the first one was put in service </s>
<s> [Figure 4] At noon we stepped ashore and bought some bottled beer and got some chickens cooked, while the raft waited; then we immediately put to sea again, and had our dinner while the beer was cold and the chickens hot </s>
<s> There is no pleasanter place for such a meal than a raft that is gliding down the winding Neckar past green meadows and wooded hills, and slumbering villages, and craggy heights graced with crumbling towers and battlements </s>
<s> In one place we saw a nicely dressed German gentleman without any spectacles </s>
<s> Before I could come to anchor he had got underway </s>
<s> It was a great pity </s>
<s> I so wanted to make a sketch of him </s>
<s> The captain comforted me for my loss, however, by saying that the man was without any doubt a fraud who had spectacles, but kept them in his pocket in order to make himself conspicuous </s>
<s> Below Hassmersheim we passed Hornberg, Goetz von Berlichingen's old castle </s>
<s> It stands on a bold elevation two hundred feet above the surface of the river; it has high vine-clad walls enclosing trees, and a peaked tower about seventy-five feet high </s>
<s> The steep hillside, from the castle clear down to the water's edge, is terraced, and clothed thick with grape vines </s>
<s> This is like farming a mansard roof </s>
<s> All the steeps along that part of the river which furnish the proper exposure, are given up to the grape </s>
<s> That region is a great producer of Rhine wines </s>
<s> The Germans are exceedingly fond of Rhine wines; they are put up in tall, slender bottles, and are considered a pleasant beverage </s>
<s> One tells them from vinegar by the label </s>
<s> The Hornberg hill is to be tunneled, and the new railway will pass under the castle </s>
<s> THE CAVE OF THE SPECTER Two miles below Hornberg castle is a cave in a low cliff, which the captain of the raft said had once been occupied by a beautiful heiress of Hornberg--the Lady Gertrude--in the old times </s>
<s> It was seven hundred years ago </s>
<s> She had a number of rich and noble lovers and one poor and obscure one, Sir Wendel Lobenfeld </s>
<s> With the native chuckleheadedness of the heroine of romance, she preferred the poor and obscure lover </s>
<s> With the native sound judgment of the father of a heroine of romance, the von Berlichingen of that day shut his daughter up in his donjon keep, or his oubliette, or his culverin, or some such place, and resolved that she should stay there until she selected a husband from among her rich and noble lovers </s>
<s> The latter visited her and persecuted her with their supplications, but without effect, for her heart was true to her poor despised Crusader, who was fighting in the Holy Land </s>
<s> Finally, she resolved that she would endure the attentions of the rich lovers no longer; so one stormy night she escaped and went down the river and hid herself in the cave on the other side </s>
<s> Her father ransacked the country for her, but found not a trace of her </s>
<s> As the days went by, and still no tidings of her came, his conscience began to torture him, and he caused proclamation to be made that if she were yet living and would return, he would oppose her no longer, she might marry whom she would </s>
<s> The months dragged on, all hope forsook the old man, he ceased from his customary pursuits and pleasures, he devoted himself to pious works, and longed for the deliverance of death </s>
<s> Now just at midnight, every night, the lost heiress stood in the mouth of her cave, arrayed in white robes, and sang a little love ballad which her Crusader had made for her </s>
<s> She judged that if he came home alive the superstitious peasants would tell him about the ghost that sang in the cave, and that as soon as they described the ballad he would know that none but he and she knew that song, therefore he would suspect that she was alive, and would come and find her </s>
<s> As time went on, the people of the region became sorely distressed about the Specter of the Haunted Cave </s>
<s> It was said that ill luck of one kind or another always overtook any one who had the misfortune to hear that song </s>
<s> Eventually, every calamity that happened thereabouts was laid at the door of that music </s>
<s> Consequently, no boatmen would consent to pass the cave at night; the peasants shunned the place, even in the daytime </s>
<s> But the faithful girl sang on, night after night, month after month, and patiently waited; her reward must come at last </s>
<s> Five years dragged by, and still, every night at midnight, the plaintive tones floated out over the silent land, while the distant boatmen and peasants thrust their fingers into their ears and shuddered out a prayer </s>
<s> And now came the Crusader home, bronzed and battle-scarred, but bringing a great and splendid fame to lay at the feet of his bride </s>
<s> The old lord of Hornberg received him as his son, and wanted him to stay by him and be the comfort and blessing of his age; but the tale of that young girl's devotion to him and its pathetic consequences made a changed man of the knight </s>
<s> He could not enjoy his well-earned rest </s>
<s> He said his heart was broken, he would give the remnant of his life to high deeds in the cause of humanity, and so find a worthy death and a blessed reunion with the brave true heart whose love had more honored him than all his victories in war </s>
<s> When the people heard this resolve of his, they came and told him there was a pitiless dragon in human disguise in the Haunted Cave, a dread creature which no knight had yet been bold enough to face, and begged him to rid the land of its desolating presence </s>
<s> He said he would do it </s>
<s> They told him about the song, and when he asked what song it was, they said the memory of it was gone, for nobody had been hardy enough to listen to it for the past four years and more </s>
<s> Toward midnight the Crusader came floating down the river in a boat, with his trusty cross-bow in his hands </s>
<s> He drifted silently through the dim reflections of the crags and trees, with his intent eyes fixed upon the low cliff which he was approaching </s>
<s> As he drew nearer, he discerned the black mouth of the cave </s>
<s> Now--is that a white figure </s>
<s> Yes </s>
<s> The plaintive song begins to well forth and float away over meadow and river--the cross-bow is slowly raised to position, a steady aim is taken, the bolt flies straight to the mark--the figure sinks down, still singing, the knight takes the wool out of his ears, and recognizes the old ballad--too late </s>
<s> Ah, if he had only not put the wool in his ears </s>
<s> The Crusader went away to the wars again, and presently fell in battle, fighting for the Cross </s>
<s> Tradition says that during several centuries the spirit of the unfortunate girl sang nightly from the cave at midnight, but the music carried no curse with it; and although many listened for the mysterious sounds, few were favored, since only those could hear them who had never failed in a trust </s>
<s> It is believed that the singing still continues, but it is known that nobody has heard it during the present century </s>
<s> CHAPTER XVI An Ancient Legend of the Rhine [The Lorelei] The last legend reminds one of the "Lorelei"--a legend of the Rhine </s>
<s> There is a song called "The Lorelei" </s>
<s> Germany is rich in folk-songs, and the words and airs of several of them are peculiarly beautiful--but "The Lorelei" is the people's favorite </s>
<s> I could not endure it at first, but by and by it began to take hold of me, and now there is no tune which I like so well </s>
<s> It is not possible that it is much known in America, else I should have heard it there </s>
<s> The fact that I never heard it there, is evidence that there are others in my country who have fared likewise; therefore, for the sake of these, I mean to print the words and music in this chapter </s>
<s> And I will refresh the reader's memory by printing the legend of the Lorelei, too </s>
<s> I have it by me in the LEGENDS OF THE RHINE, done into English by the wildly gifted Garnham, Bachelor of Arts </s>
<s> I print the legend partly to refresh my own memory, too, for I have never read it before </s>
<s> THE LEGEND Lore (two syllables) was a water nymph who used to sit on a high rock called the Ley or Lei (pronounced like our word LIE) in the Rhine, and lure boatmen to destruction in a furious rapid which marred the channel at that spot </s>
<s> She so bewitched them with her plaintive songs and her wonderful beauty that they forgot everything else to gaze up at her, and so they presently drifted among the broken reefs and were lost </s>
<s> In those old, old times, the Count Bruno lived in a great castle near there with his son, the Count Hermann, a youth of twenty </s>
<s> Hermann had heard a great deal about the beautiful Lore, and had finally fallen very deeply in love with her without having seen her </s>
<s> So he used to wander to the neighborhood of the Lei, evenings, with his Zither and "Express his Longing in low Singing," as Garnham says </s>
<s> On one of these occasions, "suddenly there hovered around the top of the rock a brightness of unequaled clearness and color, which, in increasingly smaller circles thickened, was the enchanting figure of the beautiful Lore </s>
<s> "An unintentional cry of Joy escaped the Youth, he let his Zither fall, and with extended arms he called out the name of the enigmatical Being, who seemed to stoop lovingly to him and beckon to him in a friendly manner; indeed, if his ear did not deceive him, she called his name with unutterable sweet Whispers, proper to love </s>
<s> Beside himself with delight the youth lost his Senses and sank senseless to the earth" </s>
<s> After that he was a changed person </s>
<s> He went dreaming about, thinking only of his fairy and caring for naught else in the world </s>
<s> "The old count saw with affliction this changement in his son," whose cause he could not divine, and tried to divert his mind into cheerful channels, but to no purpose </s>
<s> Then the old count used authority </s>
<s> He commanded the youth to betake himself to the camp </s>
<s> Obedience was promised </s>
<s> Garnham says: "It was on the evening before his departure, as he wished still once to visit the Lei and offer to the Nymph of the Rhine his Sighs, the tones of his Zither, and his Songs </s>
<s> He went, in his boat, this time accompanied by a faithful squire, down the stream </s>
<s> The moon shed her silvery light over the whole country; the steep bank mountains appeared in the most fantastical shapes, and the high oaks on either side bowed their Branches on Hermann's passing </s>
<s> As soon as he approached the Lei, and was aware of the surf-waves, his attendant was seized with an inexpressible Anxiety and he begged permission to land; but the Knight swept the strings of his Guitar and sang: "Once I saw thee in dark night, In supernatural Beauty bright; Of Light-rays, was the Figure wove, To share its light, locked-hair strove </s>
<s> "Thy Garment color wave-dove By thy hand the sign of love, Thy eyes sweet enchantment, Raying to me, oh </s>
<s> enchantment </s>
<s> "O, wert thou but my sweetheart, How willingly thy love to part </s>
<s> With delight I should be bound To thy rocky house in deep ground" </s>
<s> That Hermann should have gone to that place at all, was not wise; that he should have gone with such a song as that in his mouth was a most serious mistake </s>
<s> The Lorelei did not "call his name in unutterable sweet Whispers" this time </s>
<s> No, that song naturally worked an instant and thorough "changement" in her; and not only that, but it stirred the bowels of the whole afflicted region around about there--for-- "Scarcely had these tones sounded, everywhere there began tumult and sound, as if voices above and below the water </s>
<s> On the Lei rose flames, the Fairy stood above, at that time, and beckoned with her right hand clearly and urgently to the infatuated Knight, while with a staff in her left hand she called the waves to her service </s>
<s> They began to mount heavenward; the boat was upset, mocking every exertion; the waves rose to the gunwale, and splitting on the hard stones, the Boat broke into Pieces </s>
<s> The youth sank into the depths, but the squire was thrown on shore by a powerful wave" </s>
<s> The bitterest things have been said about the Lorelei during many centuries, but surely her conduct upon this occasion entitles her to our respect </s>
<s> One feels drawn tenderly toward her and is moved to forget her many crimes and remember only the good deed that crowned and closed her career </s>
<s> "The Fairy was never more seen; but her enchanting tones have often been heard </s>
<s> In the beautiful, refreshing, still nights of spring, when the moon pours her silver light over the Country, the listening shipper hears from the rushing of the waves, the echoing Clang of a wonderfully charming voice, which sings a song from the crystal castle, and with sorrow and fear he thinks on the young Count Hermann, seduced by the Nymph" </s>
<s> Here is the music, and the German words by Heinrich Heine </s>
<s> This song has been a favorite in Germany for forty years, and will remain a favorite always, maybe </s>
<s> [Figure 5] I have a prejudice against people who print things in a foreign language and add no translation </s>
<s> When I am the reader, and the author considers me able to do the translating myself, he pays me quite a nice compliment--but if he would do the translating for me I would try to get along without the compliment </s>
<s> If I were at home, no doubt I could get a translation of this poem, but I am abroad and can't; therefore I will make a translation myself </s>
<s> It may not be a good one, for poetry is out of my line, but it will serve my purpose--which is, to give the unGerman young girl a jingle of words to hang the tune on until she can get hold of a good version, made by some one who is a poet and knows how to convey a poetical thought from one language to another </s>
<s> THE LORELEI I cannot divine what it meaneth, This haunting nameless pain: A tale of the bygone ages Keeps brooding through my brain: The faint air cools in the glooming, And peaceful flows the Rhine, The thirsty summits are drinking The sunset's flooding wine; The loveliest maiden is sitting High-throned in yon blue air, Her golden jewels are shining, She combs her golden hair; She combs with a comb that is golden, And sings a weird refrain That steeps in a deadly enchantment The list'ner's ravished brain: The doomed in his drifting shallop, Is tranced with the sad sweet tone, He sees not the yawning breakers, He sees but the maid alone: The pitiless billows engulf him!-- So perish sailor and bark; And this, with her baleful singing, Is the Lorelei's gruesome work </s>
<s> I have a translation by Garnham, Bachelor of Arts, in the LEGENDS OF THE RHINE, but it would not answer the purpose I mentioned above, because the measure is too nobly irregular; it don't fit the tune snugly enough; in places it hangs over at the ends too far, and in other places one runs out of words before he gets to the end of a bar </s>
<s> Still, Garnham's translation has high merits, and I am not dreaming of leaving it out of my book </s>

<s> CHAPTER XVII [Why Germans Wear Spectacles] A mile or two above Eberbach we saw a peculiar ruin projecting above the foliage which clothed the peak of a high and very steep hill </s>
<s> This ruin consisted of merely a couple of crumbling masses of masonry which bore a rude resemblance to human faces; they leaned forward and touched foreheads, and had the look of being absorbed in conversation </s>
<s> This ruin had nothing very imposing or picturesque about it, and there was no great deal of it, yet it was called the "Spectacular Ruin" </s>
<s> LEGEND OF THE "SPECTACULAR RUIN" The captain of the raft, who was as full of history as he could stick, said that in the Middle Ages a most prodigious fire-breathing dragon used to live in that region, and made more trouble than a tax-collector </s>
<s> He was as long as a railway-train, and had the customary impenetrable green scales all over him </s>
<s> His breath bred pestilence and conflagration, and his appetite bred famine </s>
<s> He ate men and cattle impartially, and was exceedingly unpopular </s>
<s> The German emperor of that day made the usual offer: he would grant to the destroyer of the dragon, any one solitary thing he might ask for; for he had a surplusage of daughters, and it was customary for dragon-killers to take a daughter for pay </s>
<s> So the most renowned knights came from the four corners of the earth and retired down the dragon's throat one after the other </s>
<s> A panic arose and spread </s>
<s> Heroes grew cautious </s>
<s> The procession ceased </s>
<s> The dragon became more destructive than ever </s>
<s> The people lost all hope of succor, and fled to the mountains for refuge </s>
<s> At last Sir Wissenschaft, a poor and obscure knight, out of a far country, arrived to do battle with the monster </s>
<s> A pitiable object he was, with his armor hanging in rags about him, and his strange-shaped knapsack strapped upon his back </s>
<s> Everybody turned up their noses at him, and some openly jeered him </s>
<s> But he was calm </s>
<s> He simply inquired if the emperor's offer was still in force </s>
<s> The emperor said it was--but charitably advised him to go and hunt hares and not endanger so precious a life as his in an attempt which had brought death to so many of the world's most illustrious heroes </s>
<s> But this tramp only asked--"Were any of these heroes men of science" </s>
<s> This raised a laugh, of course, for science was despised in those days </s>
<s> But the tramp was not in the least ruffled </s>
<s> He said he might be a little in advance of his age, but no matter--science would come to be honored, some time or other </s>
<s> He said he would march against the dragon in the morning </s>
<s> Out of compassion, then, a decent spear was offered him, but he declined, and said, "spears were useless to men of science" </s>
<s> They allowed him to sup in the servants' hall, and gave him a bed in the stables </s>
<s> When he started forth in the morning, thousands were gathered to see </s>
<s> The emperor said: "Do not be rash, take a spear, and leave off your knapsack" </s>
<s> But the tramp said: "It is not a knapsack," and moved straight on </s>
<s> The dragon was waiting and ready </s>
<s> He was breathing forth vast volumes of sulphurous smoke and lurid blasts of flame </s>
<s> The ragged knight stole warily to a good position, then he unslung his cylindrical knapsack--which was simply the common fire-extinguisher known to modern times--and the first chance he got he turned on his hose and shot the dragon square in the center of his cavernous mouth </s>
<s> Out went the fires in an instant, and the dragon curled up and died </s>
<s> This man had brought brains to his aid </s>
<s> He had reared dragons from the egg, in his laboratory, he had watched over them like a mother, and patiently studied them and experimented upon them while they grew </s>
<s> Thus he had found out that fire was the life principle of a dragon; put out the dragon's fires and it could make steam no longer, and must die </s>
<s> He could not put out a fire with a spear, therefore he invented the extinguisher </s>
<s> The dragon being dead, the emperor fell on the hero's neck and said: "Deliverer, name your request," at the same time beckoning out behind with his heel for a detachment of his daughters to form and advance </s>
<s> But the tramp gave them no observance </s>
<s> He simply said: "My request is, that upon me be conferred the monopoly of the manufacture and sale of spectacles in Germany" </s>
<s> The emperor sprang aside and exclaimed: "This transcends all the impudence I ever heard </s>
<s> A modest demand, by my halidome </s>
<s> Why didn't you ask for the imperial revenues at once, and be done with it" </s>
<s> But the monarch had given his word, and he kept it </s>
<s> To everybody's surprise, the unselfish monopolist immediately reduced the price of spectacles to such a degree that a great and crushing burden was removed from the nation </s>
<s> The emperor, to commemorate this generous act, and to testify his appreciation of it, issued a decree commanding everybody to buy this benefactor's spectacles and wear them, whether they needed them or not </s>
<s> So originated the wide-spread custom of wearing spectacles in Germany; and as a custom once established in these old lands is imperishable, this one remains universal in the empire to this day </s>
<s> Such is the legend of the monopolist's once stately and sumptuous castle, now called the "Spectacular Ruin" </s>
<s> On the right bank, two or three miles below the Spectacular Ruin, we passed by a noble pile of castellated buildings overlooking the water from the crest of a lofty elevation </s>
<s> A stretch of two hundred yards of the high front wall was heavily draped with ivy, and out of the mass of buildings within rose three picturesque old towers </s>

<s> It did no other harm, but we took to the water just the same </s>
<s> It seems that the heavy work in the quarries and the new railway gradings is done mainly by Italians </s>

<s> They were as trim and snug and pretty as they could be </s>
<s> They were always of brick or stone; they were of graceful shape, they had vines and flowers about them already, and around them the grass was bright and green, and showed that it was carefully looked after </s>
<s> They were a decoration to the beautiful landscape, not an offense </s>
<s> Wherever one saw a pile of gravel or a pile of broken stone, it was always heaped as trimly and exactly as a new grave or a stack of cannon-balls; nothing about those stations or along the railroad or the wagon-road was allowed to look shabby or be unornamental </s>
<s> The keeping a country in such beautiful order as Germany exhibits, has a wise practical side to it, too, for it keeps thousands of people in work and bread who would otherwise be idle and mischievous </s>

<s> We tramped through the darkness and the drenching summer rain full three miles, and reached "The Naturalist Tavern" in the village of Hirschhorn just an hour before midnight, almost exhausted from hardship, fatigue, and terror </s>

<s> The landlord was rich, and therefore could afford to be crusty and disobliging; he did not at all like being turned out of his warm bed to open his house for us </s>

<s> Such rooms and beds and embroidered linen are as frequent in German village inns as they are rare in ours </s>
<s> Our villages are superior to German villages in more merits, excellences, conveniences, and privileges than I can enumerate, but the hotels do not belong in the list </s>
<s> "The Naturalist Tavern" was not a meaningless name; for all the halls and all the rooms were lined with large glass cases which were filled with all sorts of birds and animals, glass-eyed, ably stuffed, and set up in the most natural eloquent and dramatic attitudes </s>
<s> The moment we were abed, the rain cleared away and the moon came out </s>
<s> I dozed off to sleep while contemplating a great white stuffed owl which was looking intently down on me from a high perch with the air of a person who thought he had met me before, but could not make out for certain </s>
<s> But young Z did not get off so easily </s>
<s> He said that as he was sinking deliciously to sleep, the moon lifted away the shadows and developed a huge cat, on a bracket, dead and stuffed, but crouching, with every muscle tense, for a spring, and with its glittering glass eyes aimed straight at him </s>
<s> It made Z uncomfortable </s>
<s> He tried closing his own eyes, but that did not answer, for a natural instinct kept making him open them again to see if the cat was still getting ready to launch at him--which she always was </s>
<s> He tried turning his back, but that was a failure; he knew the sinister eyes were on him still </s>
<s> So at last he had to get up, after an hour or two of worry and experiment, and set the cat out in the hall </s>
<s> So he won, that time </s>
<s> CHAPTER XVIII [The Kindly Courtesy of Germans] In the morning we took breakfast in the garden, under the trees, in the delightful German summer fashion </s>
<s> The air was filled with the fragrance of flowers and wild animals; the living portion of the menagerie of the "Naturalist Tavern" was all about us </s>
<s> There were great cages populous with fluttering and chattering foreign birds, and other great cages and greater wire pens, populous with quadrupeds, both native and foreign </s>
<s> There were some free creatures, too, and quite sociable ones they were </s>
<s> White rabbits went loping about the place, and occasionally came and sniffed at our shoes and shins; a fawn, with a red ribbon on its neck, walked up and examined us fearlessly; rare breeds of chickens and doves begged for crumbs, and a poor old tailless raven hopped about with a humble, shamefaced mein which said, "Please do not notice my exposure--think how you would feel in my circumstances, and be charitable" </s>
<s> If he was observed too much, he would retire behind something and stay there until he judged the party's interest had found another object </s>
<s> I never have seen another dumb creature that was so morbidly sensitive </s>
<s> Bayard Taylor, who could interpret the dim reasonings of animals, and understood their moral natures better than most men, would have found some way to make this poor old chap forget his troubles for a while, but we have not his kindly art, and so had to leave the raven to his griefs </s>
<s> After breakfast we climbed the hill and visited the ancient castle of Hirschhorn, and the ruined church near it </s>
<s> There were some curious old bas-reliefs leaning against the inner walls of the church--sculptured lords of Hirschhorn in complete armor, and ladies of Hirschhorn in the picturesque court costumes of the Middle Ages </s>
<s> These things are suffering damage and passing to decay, for the last Hirschhorn has been dead two hundred years, and there is nobody now who cares to preserve the family relics </s>
<s> In the chancel was a twisted stone column, and the captain told us a legend about it, of course, for in the matter of legends he could not seem to restrain himself; but I do not repeat his tale because there was nothing plausible about it except that the Hero wrenched this column into its present screw-shape with his hands --just one single wrench </s>
<s> All the rest of the legend was doubtful </s>
<s> But Hirschhorn is best seen from a distance, down the river </s>
<s> Then the clustered brown towers perched on the green hilltop, and the old battlemented stone wall, stretching up and over the grassy ridge and disappearing in the leafy sea beyond, make a picture whose grace and beauty entirely satisfy the eye </s>
<s> We descended from the church by steep stone stairways which curved this way and that down narrow alleys between the packed and dirty tenements of the village </s>
<s> It was a quarter well stocked with deformed, leering, unkempt and uncombed idiots, who held out hands or caps and begged piteously </s>
<s> The people of the quarter were not all idiots, of course, but all that begged seemed to be, and were said to be </s>
<s> I was thinking of going by skiff to the next town, Necharsteinach; so I ran to the riverside in advance of the party and asked a man there if he had a boat to hire </s>
<s> I suppose I must have spoken High German--Court German--I intended it for that, anyway--so he did not understand me </s>
<s> I turned and twisted my question around and about, trying to strike that man's average, but failed </s>
<s> He could not make out what I wanted </s>
<s> Now Mr X arrived, faced this same man, looked him in the eye, and emptied this sentence on him, in the most glib and confident way: "Can man boat get here" </s>
<s> The mariner promptly understood and promptly answered </s>
<s> I can comprehend why he was able to understand that particular sentence, because by mere accident all the words in it except "get" have the same sound and the same meaning in German that they have in English; but how he managed to understand Mr X's next remark puzzled me </s>
<s> I will insert it, presently </s>
<s> X turned away a moment, and I asked the mariner if he could not find a board, and so construct an additional seat </s>
<s> I spoke in the purest German, but I might as well have spoken in the purest Choctaw for all the good it did </s>
<s> The man tried his best to understand me; he tried, and kept on trying, harder and harder, until I saw it was really of no use, and said: "There, don't strain yourself--it is of no consequence" </s>
<s> Then X turned to him and crisply said: "MACHEN SIE a flat board" </s>
<s> I wish my epitaph may tell the truth about me if the man did not answer up at once, and say he would go and borrow a board as soon as he had lit the pipe which he was filling </s>
<s> We changed our mind about taking a boat, so we did not have to go </s>
<s> I have given Mr X's two remarks just as he made them </s>
<s> Four of the five words in the first one were English, and that they were also German was only accidental, not intentional; three out of the five words in the second remark were English, and English only, and the two German ones did not mean anything in particular, in such a connection </s>
<s> X always spoke English to Germans, but his plan was to turn the sentence wrong end first and upside down, according to German construction, and sprinkle in a German word without any essential meaning to it, here and there, by way of flavor </s>
<s> Yet he always made himself understood </s>
<s> He could make those dialect-speaking raftsmen understand him, sometimes, when even young Z had failed with them; and young Z was a pretty good German scholar </s>
<s> For one thing, X always spoke with such confidence--perhaps that helped </s>
<s> And possibly the raftsmen's dialect was what is called PLATT-DEUTSCH, and so they found his English more familiar to their ears than another man's German </s>
<s> Quite indifferent students of German can read Fritz Reuter's charming platt-Deutch tales with some little facility because many of the words are English </s>
<s> I suppose this is the tongue which our Saxon ancestors carried to England with them </s>
<s> By and by I will inquire of some other philologist </s>
<s> However, in the mean time it had transpired that the men employed to calk the raft had found that the leak was not a leak at all, but only a crack between the logs--a crack that belonged there, and was not dangerous, but had been magnified into a leak by the disordered imagination of the mate </s>
<s> Therefore we went aboard again with a good degree of confidence, and presently got to sea without accident </s>
<s> As we swam smoothly along between the enchanting shores, we fell to swapping notes about manners and customs in Germany and elsewhere </s>
<s> As I write, now, many months later, I perceive that each of us, by observing and noting and inquiring, diligently and day by day, had managed to lay in a most varied and opulent stock of misinformation </s>
<s> But this is not surprising; it is very difficult to get accurate details in any country </s>
<s> For example, I had the idea once, in Heidelberg, to find out all about those five student-corps </s>
<s> I started with the White Cap corps </s>
<s> I began to inquire of this and that and the other citizen, and here is what I found out: 1 </s>
<s> It is called the Prussian Corps, because none but Prussians are admitted to it </s>
<s> 2 </s>
<s> It is called the Prussian Corps for no particular reason </s>
<s> It has simply pleased each corps to name itself after some German state </s>
<s> 3 </s>
<s> It is not named the Prussian Corps at all, but only the White Cap Corps </s>
<s> 4 </s>
<s> Any student can belong to it who is a German by birth </s>
<s> 5 </s>
<s> Any student can belong to it who is European by birth </s>
<s> 6 </s>
<s> Any European-born student can belong to it, except he be a Frenchman </s>
<s> 7 </s>
<s> Any student can belong to it, no matter where he was born </s>
<s> 8 </s>
<s> No student can belong to it who is not of noble blood </s>
<s> 9 </s>
<s> No student can belong to it who cannot show three full generations of noble descent </s>
<s> 10 </s>
<s> Nobility is not a necessary qualification </s>
<s> 11 </s>
<s> No moneyless student can belong to it </s>
<s> 12 </s>
<s> Money qualification is nonsense--such a thing has never been thought of </s>
<s> I got some of this information from students themselves--students who did not belong to the corps </s>
<s> I finally went to headquarters--to the White Caps--where I would have gone in the first place if I had been acquainted </s>
<s> But even at headquarters I found difficulties; I perceived that there were things about the White Cap Corps which one member knew and another one didn't </s>
<s> It was natural; for very few members of any organization know ALL that can be known about it </s>
<s> I doubt there is a man or a woman in Heidelberg who would not answer promptly and confidently three out of every five questions about the White Cap Corps which a stranger might ask; yet it is a very safe bet that two of the three answers would be incorrect every time </s>
<s> There is one German custom which is universal--the bowing courteously to strangers when sitting down at table or rising up from it </s>
<s> This bow startles a stranger out of his self-possession, the first time it occurs, and he is likely to fall over a chair or something, in his embarrassment, but it pleases him, nevertheless </s>
<s> One soon learns to expect this bow and be on the lookout and ready to return it; but to learn to lead off and make the initial bow one's self is a difficult matter for a diffident man </s>
<s> One thinks, "If I rise to go, and tender my bow, and these ladies and gentlemen take it into their heads to ignore the custom of their nation, and not return it, how shall I feel, in case I survive to feel anything" </s>
<s> Therefore he is afraid to venture </s>
<s> He sits out the dinner, and makes the strangers rise first and originate the bowing </s>
<s> A table d'hôte dinner is a tedious affair for a man who seldom touches anything after the three first courses; therefore I used to do some pretty dreary waiting because of my fears </s>
<s> It took me months to assure myself that those fears were groundless, but I did assure myself at last by experimenting diligently through my agent </s>
<s> I made Harris get up and bow and leave; invariably his bow was returned, then I got up and bowed myself and retired </s>
<s> Thus my education proceeded easily and comfortably for me, but not for Harris </s>
<s> Three courses of a table d'hôte dinner were enough for me, but Harris preferred thirteen </s>
<s> Even after I had acquired full confidence, and no longer needed the agent's help, I sometimes encountered difficulties </s>
<s> Once at Baden-Baden I nearly lost a train because I could not be sure that three young ladies opposite me at table were Germans, since I had not heard them speak; they might be American, they might be English, it was not safe to venture a bow; but just as I had got that far with my thought, one of them began a German remark, to my great relief and gratitude; and before she got out her third word, our bows had been delivered and graciously returned, and we were off </s>
<s> There is a friendly something about the German character which is very winning </s>
<s> When Harris and I were making a pedestrian tour through the Black Forest, we stopped at a little country inn for dinner one day; two young ladies and a young gentleman entered and sat down opposite us </s>
<s> They were pedestrians, too </s>
<s> Our knapsacks were strapped upon our backs, but they had a sturdy youth along to carry theirs for them </s>
<s> All parties were hungry, so there was no talking </s>
<s> By and by the usual bows were exchanged, and we separated </s>
<s> As we sat at a late breakfast in the hotel at Allerheiligen, next morning, these young people entered and took places near us without observing us; but presently they saw us and at once bowed and smiled; not ceremoniously, but with the gratified look of people who have found acquaintances where they were expecting strangers </s>
<s> Then they spoke of the weather and the roads </s>
<s> We also spoke of the weather and the roads </s>
<s> Next, they said they had had an enjoyable walk, notwithstanding the weather </s>
<s> We said that that had been our case, too </s>
<s> Then they said they had walked thirty English miles the day before, and asked how many we had walked </s>
<s> I could not lie, so I told Harris to do it </s>
<s> Harris told them we had made thirty English miles, too </s>
<s> That was true; we had "made" them, though we had had a little assistance here and there </s>
<s> After breakfast they found us trying to blast some information out of the dumb hotel clerk about routes, and observing that we were not succeeding pretty well, they went and got their maps and things, and pointed out and explained our course so clearly that even a New York detective could have followed it </s>
<s> And when we started they spoke out a hearty good-by and wished us a pleasant journey </s>
<s> Perhaps they were more generous with us than they might have been with native wayfarers because we were a forlorn lot and in a strange land; I don't know; I only know it was lovely to be treated so </s>
<s> Very well, I took an American young lady to one of the fine balls in Baden-Baden, one night, and at the entrance-door upstairs we were halted by an official--something about Miss Jones's dress was not according to rule; I don't remember what it was, now; something was wanting--her back hair, or a shawl, or a fan, or a shovel, or something </s>
<s> The official was ever so polite, and ever so sorry, but the rule was strict, and he could not let us in </s>
<s> It was very embarrassing, for many eyes were on us </s>
<s> But now a richly dressed girl stepped out of the ballroom, inquired into the trouble, and said she could fix it in a moment </s>
<s> She took Miss Jones to the robing-room, and soon brought her back in regulation trim, and then we entered the ballroom with this benefactress unchallenged </s>
<s> Being safe, now, I began to puzzle through my sincere but ungrammatical thanks, when there was a sudden mutual recognition --the benefactress and I had met at Allerheiligen </s>
<s> Two weeks had not altered her good face, and plainly her heart was in the right place yet, but there was such a difference between these clothes and the clothes I had seen her in before, when she was walking thirty miles a day in the Black Forest, that it was quite natural that I had failed to recognize her sooner </s>
<s> I had on MY other suit, too, but my German would betray me to a person who had heard it once, anyway </s>
<s> She brought her brother and sister, and they made our way smooth for that evening </s>
<s> Well--months afterward, I was driving through the streets of Munich in a cab with a German lady, one day, when she said: "There, that is Prince Ludwig and his wife, walking along there" </s>
<s> Everybody was bowing to them--cabmen, little children, and everybody else--and they were returning all the bows and overlooking nobody, when a young lady met them and made a deep courtesy </s>
<s> "That is probably one of the ladies of the court," said my German friend </s>
<s> I said: "She is an honor to it, then </s>
<s> I know her </s>
<s> I don't know her name, but I know HER </s>
<s> I have known her at Allerheiligen and Baden-Baden </s>
<s> She ought to be an Empress, but she may be only a Duchess; it is the way things go in this way" </s>
<s> If one asks a German a civil question, he will be quite sure to get a civil answer </s>
<s> If you stop a German in the street and ask him to direct you to a certain place, he shows no sign of feeling offended </s>
<s> If the place be difficult to find, ten to one the man will drop his own matters and go with you and show you </s>
<s> In London, too, many a time, strangers have walked several blocks with me to show me my way </s>
<s> There is something very real about this sort of politeness </s>
<s> Quite often, in Germany, shopkeepers who could not furnish me the article I wanted have sent one of their employees with me to show me a place where it could be had </s>
<s> CHAPTER XIX [The Deadly Jest of Dilsberg] However, I wander from the raft </s>
<s> We made the port of Necharsteinach in good season, and went to the hotel and ordered a trout dinner, the same to be ready against our return from a two-hour pedestrian excursion to the village and castle of Dilsberg, a mile distant, on the other side of the river </s>
<s> I do not mean that we proposed to be two hours making two miles--no, we meant to employ most of the time in inspecting Dilsberg </s>
<s> For Dilsberg is a quaint place </s>
<s> It is most quaintly and picturesquely situated, too </s>
<s> Imagine the beautiful river before you; then a few rods of brilliant green sward on its opposite shore; then a sudden hill--no preparatory gently rising slopes, but a sort of instantaneous hill--a hill two hundred and fifty or three hundred feet high, as round as a bowl, with the same taper upward that an inverted bowl has, and with about the same relation of height to diameter that distinguishes a bowl of good honest depth--a hill which is thickly clothed with green bushes--a comely, shapely hill, rising abruptly out of the dead level of the surrounding green plains, visible from a great distance down the bends of the river, and with just exactly room on the top of its head for its steepled and turreted and roof-clustered cap of architecture, which same is tightly jammed and compacted within the perfectly round hoop of the ancient village wall </s>
<s> There is no house outside the wall on the whole hill, or any vestige of a former house; all the houses are inside the wall, but there isn't room for another one </s>
<s> It is really a finished town, and has been finished a very long time </s>
<s> There is no space between the wall and the first circle of buildings; no, the village wall is itself the rear wall of the first circle of buildings, and the roofs jut a little over the wall and thus furnish it with eaves </s>
<s> The general level of the massed roofs is gracefully broken and relieved by the dominating towers of the ruined castle and the tall spires of a couple of churches; so, from a distance Dilsberg has rather more the look of a king's crown than a cap </s>
<s> That lofty green eminence and its quaint coronet form quite a striking picture, you may be sure, in the flush of the evening sun </s>
<s> We crossed over in a boat and began the ascent by a narrow, steep path which plunged us at once into the leafy deeps of the bushes </s>
<s> But they were not cool deeps by any means, for the sun's rays were weltering hot and there was little or no breeze to temper them </s>
<s> As we panted up the sharp ascent, we met brown, bareheaded and barefooted boys and girls, occasionally, and sometimes men; they came upon us without warning, they gave us good day, flashed out of sight in the bushes, and were gone as suddenly and mysteriously as they had come </s>
<s> They were bound for the other side of the river to work </s>
<s> This path had been traveled by many generations of these people </s>
<s> They have always gone down to the valley to earn their bread, but they have always climbed their hill again to eat it, and to sleep in their snug town </s>
<s> It is said that the Dilsbergers do not emigrate much; they find that living up there above the world, in their peaceful nest, is pleasanter than living down in the troublous world </s>
<s> The seven hundred inhabitants are all blood-kin to each other, too; they have always been blood-kin to each other for fifteen hundred years; they are simply one large family, and they like the home folks better than they like strangers, hence they persistently stay at home </s>
<s> It has been said that for ages Dilsberg has been merely a thriving and diligent idiot-factory </s>
<s> I saw no idiots there, but the captain said, "Because of late years the government has taken to lugging them off to asylums and otherwheres; and government wants to cripple the factory, too, and is trying to get these Dilsbergers to marry out of the family, but they don't like to" </s>
<s> The captain probably imagined all this, as modern science denies that the intermarrying of relatives deteriorates the stock </s>
<s> Arrived within the wall, we found the usual village sights and life </s>
<s> We moved along a narrow, crooked lane which had been paved in the Middle Ages </s>
<s> A strapping, ruddy girl was beating flax or some such stuff in a little bit of a good-box of a barn, and she swung her flail with a will--if it was a flail; I was not farmer enough to know what she was at; a frowsy, barelegged girl was herding half a dozen geese with a stick--driving them along the lane and keeping them out of the dwellings; a cooper was at work in a shop which I know he did not make so large a thing as a hogshead in, for there was not room </s>
<s> In the front rooms of dwellings girls and women were cooking or spinning, and ducks and chickens were waddling in and out, over the threshold, picking up chance crumbs and holding pleasant converse; a very old and wrinkled man sat asleep before his door, with his chin upon his breast and his extinguished pipe in his lap; soiled children were playing in the dirt everywhere along the lane, unmindful of the sun </s>
<s> Except the sleeping old man, everybody was at work, but the place was very still and peaceful, nevertheless; so still that the distant cackle of the successful hen smote upon the ear but little dulled by intervening sounds </s>
<s> That commonest of village sights was lacking here--the public pump, with its great stone tank or trough of limpid water, and its group of gossiping pitcher-bearers; for there is no well or fountain or spring on this tall hill; cisterns of rain-water are used </s>
<s> Our alpenstocks and muslin tails compelled attention, and as we moved through the village we gathered a considerable procession of little boys and girls, and so went in some state to the castle </s>
<s> It proved to be an extensive pile of crumbling walls, arches, and towers, massive, properly grouped for picturesque effect, weedy, grass-grown, and satisfactory </s>
<s> The children acted as guides; they walked us along the top of the highest walls, then took us up into a high tower and showed us a wide and beautiful landscape, made up of wavy distances of woody hills, and a nearer prospect of undulating expanses of green lowlands, on the one hand, and castle-graced crags and ridges on the other, with the shining curves of the Neckar flowing between </s>
<s> But the principal show, the chief pride of the children, was the ancient and empty well in the grass-grown court of the castle </s>
<s> Its massive stone curb stands up three or four feet above-ground, and is whole and uninjured </s>
<s> The children said that in the Middle Ages this well was four hundred feet deep, and furnished all the village with an abundant supply of water, in war and peace </s>
<s> They said that in the old day its bottom was below the level of the Neckar, hence the water-supply was inexhaustible </s>
<s> But there were some who believed it had never been a well at all, and was never deeper than it is now--eighty feet; that at that depth a subterranean passage branched from it and descended gradually to a remote place in the valley, where it opened into somebody's cellar or other hidden recess, and that the secret of this locality is now lost </s>
<s> Those who hold this belief say that herein lies the explanation that Dilsberg, besieged by Tilly and many a soldier before him, was never taken: after the longest and closest sieges the besiegers were astonished to perceive that the besieged were as fat and hearty as ever, and were well furnished with munitions of war--therefore it must be that the Dilsbergers had been bringing these things in through the subterranean passage all the time </s>
<s> The children said that there was in truth a subterranean outlet down there, and they would prove it </s>
<s> So they set a great truss of straw on fire and threw it down the well, while we leaned on the curb and watched the glowing mass descend </s>
<s> It struck bottom and gradually burned out </s>
<s> No smoke came up </s>
<s> The children clapped their hands and said: "You see </s>
<s> Nothing makes so much smoke as burning straw--now where did the smoke go to, if there is no subterranean outlet" </s>
<s> So it seemed quite evident that the subterranean outlet indeed existed </s>
<s> But the finest thing within the ruin's limits was a noble linden, which the children said was four hundred years old, and no doubt it was </s>
<s> It had a mighty trunk and a mighty spread of limb and foliage </s>
<s> The limbs near the ground were nearly the thickness of a barrel </s>
<s> That tree had witnessed the assaults of men in mail--how remote such a time seems, and how ungraspable is the fact that real men ever did fight in real armor!--and it had seen the time when these broken arches and crumbling battlements were a trim and strong and stately fortress, fluttering its gay banners in the sun, and peopled with vigorous humanity--how impossibly long ago that seems!--and here it stands yet, and possibly may still be standing here, sunning itself and dreaming its historical dreams, when today shall have been joined to the days called "ancient" </s>
<s> Well, we sat down under the tree to smoke, and the captain delivered himself of his legend: THE LEGEND OF DILSBERG CASTLE It was to this effect </s>
<s> In the old times there was once a great company assembled at the castle, and festivity ran high </s>
<s> Of course there was a haunted chamber in the castle, and one day the talk fell upon that </s>
<s> It was said that whoever slept in it would not wake again for fifty years </s>
<s> Now when a young knight named Conrad von Geisberg heard this, he said that if the castle were his he would destroy that chamber, so that no foolish person might have the chance to bring so dreadful a misfortune upon himself and afflict such as loved him with the memory of it </s>
<s> Straightway, the company privately laid their heads together to contrive some way to get this superstitious young man to sleep in that chamber </s>
<s> And they succeeded--in this way </s>
<s> They persuaded his betrothed, a lovely mischievous young creature, niece of the lord of the castle, to help them in their plot </s>
<s> She presently took him aside and had speech with him </s>
<s> She used all her persuasions, but could not shake him; he said his belief was firm, that if he should sleep there he would wake no more for fifty years, and it made him shudder to think of it </s>
<s> Catharina began to weep </s>
<s> This was a better argument; Conrad could not hold out against it </s>
<s> He yielded and said she should have her wish if she would only smile and be happy again </s>
<s> She flung her arms about his neck, and the kisses she gave him showed that her thankfulness and her pleasure were very real </s>
<s> Then she flew to tell the company her success, and the applause she received made her glad and proud she had undertaken her mission, since all alone she had accomplished what the multitude had failed in </s>

<s> CHAPTER XX [My Precious, Priceless Tear-Jug] Next morning brought good news--our trunks had arrived from Hamburg at last </s>
<s> Let this be a warning to the reader </s>
<s> The Germans are very conscientious, and this trait makes them very particular </s>
<s> Therefore if you tell a German you want a thing done immediately, he takes you at your word; he thinks you mean what you say; so he does that thing immediately--according to his idea of immediately--which is about a week; that is, it is a week if it refers to the building of a garment, or it is an hour and a half if it refers to the cooking of a trout </s>
<s> Very well; if you tell a German to send your trunk to you by "slow freight," he takes you at your word; he sends it by "slow freight," and you cannot imagine how long you will go on enlarging your admiration of the expressiveness of that phrase in the German tongue, before you get that trunk </s>
<s> The hair on my trunk was soft and thick and youthful, when I got it ready for shipment in Hamburg; it was baldheaded when it reached Heidelberg </s>
<s> However, it was still sound, that was a comfort, it was not battered in the least; the baggagemen seemed to be conscientiously careful, in Germany, of the baggage entrusted to their hands </s>
<s> There was nothing now in the way of our departure, therefore we set about our preparations </s>
<s> Naturally my chief solicitude was about my collection of Ceramics </s>
<s> Of course I could not take it with me, that would be inconvenient, and dangerous besides </s>
<s> I took advice, but the best brick-a-brackers were divided as to the wisest course to pursue; some said pack the collection and warehouse it; others said try to get it into the Grand Ducal Museum at Mannheim for safe keeping </s>
<s> So I divided the collection, and followed the advice of both parties </s>
<s> I set aside, for the Museum, those articles which were the most frail and precious </s>
<s> Among these was my Etruscan tear-jug </s>
<s> I have made a little sketch of it here; that thing creeping up the side is not a bug, it is a hole </s>
<s> I bought this tear-jug of a dealer in antiquities for four hundred and fifty dollars </s>
<s> It is very rare </s>
<s> The man said the Etruscans used to keep tears or something in these things, and that it was very hard to get hold of a broken one, now </s>
<s> I also set aside my Henri II </s>
<s> plate </s>
<s> See sketch from my pencil; it is in the main correct, though I think I have foreshortened one end of it a little too much, perhaps </s>
<s> This is very fine and rare; the shape is exceedingly beautiful and unusual </s>
<s> It has wonderful decorations on it, but I am not able to reproduce them </s>
<s> It cost more than the tear-jug, as the dealer said there was not another plate just like it in the world </s>
<s> He said there was much false Henri II ware around, but that the genuineness of this piece was unquestionable </s>
<s> He showed me its pedigree, or its history, if you please; it was a document which traced this plate's movements all the way down from its birth--showed who bought it, from whom, and what he paid for it--from the first buyer down to me, whereby I saw that it had gone steadily up from thirty-five cents to seven hundred dollars </s>
<s> He said that the whole Ceramic world would be informed that it was now in my possession and would make a note of it, with the price paid </s>
<s> [Figure 8] There were Masters in those days, but, alas--it is not so now </s>
<s> Of course the main preciousness of this piece lies in its color; it is that old sensuous, pervading, ramifying, interpolating, transboreal blue which is the despair of modern art </s>
<s> The little sketch which I have made of this gem cannot and does not do it justice, since I have been obliged to leave out the color </s>
<s> But I've got the expression, though </s>
<s> However, I must not be frittering away the reader's time with these details </s>
<s> I did not intend to go into any detail at all, at first, but it is the failing of the true ceramiker, or the true devotee in any department of brick-a-brackery, that once he gets his tongue or his pen started on his darling theme, he cannot well stop until he drops from exhaustion </s>
<s> He has no more sense of the flight of time than has any other lover when talking of his sweetheart </s>
<s> The very "marks" on the bottom of a piece of rare crockery are able to throw me into a gibbering ecstasy; and I could forsake a drowning relative to help dispute about whether the stopple of a departed Buon Retiro scent-bottle was genuine or spurious </s>
<s> Many people say that for a male person, bric-a-brac hunting is about as robust a business as making doll-clothes, or decorating Japanese pots with decalcomania butterflies would be, and these people fling mud at the elegant Englishman, Byng, who wrote a book called THE BRIC-A-BRAC HUNTER, and make fun of him for chasing around after what they choose to call "his despicable trifles"; and for "gushing" over these trifles; and for exhibiting his "deep infantile delight" in what they call his "tuppenny collection of beggarly trivialities"; and for beginning his book with a picture of himself seated, in a "sappy, self-complacent attitude, in the midst of his poor little ridiculous bric-a-brac junk shop" </s>
<s> It is easy to say these things; it is easy to revile us, easy to despise us; therefore, let these people rail on; they cannot feel as Byng and I feel--it is their loss, not ours </s>

<s> CHAPTER XXI [Insolent Shopkeepers and Gabbling Americans] Baden-Baden sits in the lap of the hills, and the natural and artificial beauties of the surroundings are combined effectively and charmingly </s>
<s> The level strip of ground which stretches through and beyond the town is laid out in handsome pleasure grounds, shaded by noble trees and adorned at intervals with lofty and sparkling fountain-jets </s>
<s> Thrice a day a fine band makes music in the public promenade before the Conversation House, and in the afternoon and evening that locality is populous with fashionably dressed people of both sexes, who march back and forth past the great music-stand and look very much bored, though they make a show of feeling otherwise </s>
<s> It seems like a rather aimless and stupid existence </s>
<s> A good many of these people are there for a real purpose, however; they are racked with rheumatism, and they are there to stew it out in the hot baths </s>
<s> These invalids looked melancholy enough, limping about on their canes and crutches, and apparently brooding over all sorts of cheerless things </s>
<s> People say that Germany, with her damp stone houses, is the home of rheumatism </s>
<s> If that is so, Providence must have foreseen that it would be so, and therefore filled the land with the healing baths </s>
<s> Perhaps no other country is so generously supplied with medicinal springs as Germany </s>
<s> Some of these baths are good for one ailment, some for another; and again, peculiar ailments are conquered by combining the individual virtues of several different baths </s>
<s> For instance, for some forms of disease, the patient drinks the native hot water of Baden-Baden, with a spoonful of salt from the Carlsbad springs dissolved in it </s>
<s> That is not a dose to be forgotten right away </s>
<s> They don't SELL this hot water; no, you go into the great Trinkhalle, and stand around, first on one foot and then on the other, while two or three young girls sit pottering at some sort of ladylike sewing-work in your neighborhood and can't seem to see you --polite as three-dollar clerks in government offices </s>
<s> By and by one of these rises painfully, and "stretches"--stretches fists and body heavenward till she raises her heels from the floor, at the same time refreshing herself with a yawn of such comprehensiveness that the bulk of her face disappears behind her upper lip and one is able to see how she is constructed inside--then she slowly closes her cavern, brings down her fists and her heels, comes languidly forward, contemplates you contemptuously, draws you a glass of hot water and sets it down where you can get it by reaching for it </s>
<s> You take it and say: "How much"?--and she returns you, with elaborate indifference, a beggar's answer: "NACH BELIEBE" (what you please.) This thing of using the common beggar's trick and the common beggar's shibboleth to put you on your liberality when you were expecting a simple straightforward commercial transaction, adds a little to your prospering sense of irritation </s>
<s> You ignore her reply, and ask again: "How much" </s>
<s> --and she calmly, indifferently, repeats: "NACH BELIEBE" </s>
<s> You are getting angry, but you are trying not to show it; you resolve to keep on asking your question till she changes her answer, or at least her annoyingly indifferent manner </s>
