its Neighbors--Beauty of Soap Bubbles--A Wild Drive--The King of Drivers--Benefit of getting Drunk CHAPTER XXXVI [The Fiendish Fun of Alp-climbing] We did not oversleep at St </s>
<s> Nicholas </s>
<s> The church-bell began to ring at four-thirty in the morning, and from the length of time it continued to ring I judged that it takes the Swiss sinner a good while to get the invitation through his head </s>
<s> Most church-bells in the world are of poor quality, and have a harsh and rasping sound which upsets the temper and produces much sin, but the St </s>
<s> Nicholas bell is a good deal the worst one that has been contrived yet, and is peculiarly maddening in its operation </s>
<s> Still, it may have its right and its excuse to exist, for the community is poor and not every citizen can afford a clock, perhaps; but there cannot be any excuse for our church-bells at home, for there is no family in America without a clock, and consequently there is no fair pretext for the usual Sunday medley of dreadful sounds that issues from our steeples </s>
<s> There is much more profanity in America on Sunday than in all in the other six days of the week put together, and it is of a more bitter and malignant character than the week-day profanity, too </s>
<s> It is produced by the cracked-pot clangor of the cheap church-bells </s>
<s> We build our churches almost without regard to cost; we rear an edifice which is an adornment to the town, and we gild it, and fresco it, and mortgage it, and do everything we can think of to perfect it, and then spoil it all by putting a bell on it which afflicts everybody who hears it, giving some the headache, others St </s>
<s> Vitus's dance, and the rest the blind staggers </s>
<s> An American village at ten o'clock on a summer Sunday is the quietest and peacefulest and holiest thing in nature; but it is a pretty different thing half an hour later </s>
<s> Mr Poe's poem of the "Bells" stands incomplete to this day; but it is well enough that it is so, for the public reciter or "reader" who goes around trying to imitate the sounds of the various sorts of bells with his voice would find himself "up a stump" when he got to the church-bell--as Joseph Addison would say </s>
<s> The church is always trying to get other people to reform; it might not be a bad idea to reform itself a little, by way of example </s>
<s> It is still clinging to one or two things which were useful once, but which are not useful now, neither are they ornamental </s>
<s> One is the bell-ringing to remind a clock-caked town that it is church-time, and another is the reading from the pulpit of a tedious list of "notices" which everybody who is interested has already read in the newspaper </s>
<s> The clergyman even reads the hymn through--a relic of an ancient time when hymn-books are scarce and costly; but everybody has a hymn-book, now, and so the public reading is no longer necessary </s>
<s> It is not merely unnecessary, it is generally painful; for the average clergyman could not fire into his congregation with a shotgun and hit a worse reader than himself, unless the weapon scattered shamefully </s>
<s> I am not meaning to be flippant and irreverent, I am only meaning to be truthful </s>
<s> The average clergyman, in all countries and of all denominations, is a very bad reader </s>
<s> One would think he would at least learn how to read the Lord's Prayer, by and by, but it is not so </s>
<s> He races through it as if he thought the quicker he got it in, the sooner it would be answered </s>
<s> A person who does not appreciate the exceeding value of pauses, and does not know how to measure their duration judiciously, cannot render the grand simplicity and dignity of a composition like that effectively </s>
<s> We took a tolerably early breakfast, and tramped off toward Zermatt through the reeking lanes of the village, glad to get away from that bell </s>
<s> By and by we had a fine spectacle on our right </s>
<s> It was the wall-like butt end of a huge glacier, which looked down on us from an Alpine height which was well up in the blue sky </s>
<s> It was an astonishing amount of ice to be compacted together in one mass </s>
<s> We ciphered upon it and decided that it was not less than several hundred feet from the base of the wall of solid ice to the top of it--Harris believed it was really twice that </s>
<s> We judged that if St </s>
<s> Paul's, St </s>
<s> Peter's, the Great Pyramid, the Strasburg Cathedral and the Capitol in Washington were clustered against that wall, a man sitting on its upper edge could not hang his hat on the top of any one of them without reaching down three or four hundred feet--a thing which, of course, no man could do </s>
<s> To me, that mighty glacier was very beautiful </s>
<s> I did not imagine that anybody could find fault with it; but I was mistaken </s>
<s> Harris had been snarling for several days </s>
<s> He was a rabid Protestant, and he was always saying: "In the Protestant cantons you never see such poverty and dirt and squalor as you do in this Catholic one; you never see the lanes and alleys flowing with foulness; you never see such wretched little sties of houses; you never see an inverted tin turnip on top of a church for a dome; and as for a church-bell, why, you never hear a church-bell at all" </s>
<s> All this morning he had been finding fault, straight along </s>
<s> First it was with the mud </s>
<s> He said, "It ain't muddy in a Protestant canton when it rains" </s>
<s> Then it was with the dogs: "They don't have those lop-eared dogs in a Protestant canton" </s>
<s> Then it was with the roads: "They don't leave the roads to make themselves in a Protestant canton, the people make them--and they make a road that IS a road, too" </s>
<s> Next it was the goats: "You never see a goat shedding tears in a Protestant canton--a goat, there, is one of the cheerfulest objects in nature" </s>
<s> Next it was the chamois: "You never see a Protestant chamois act like one of these--they take a bite or two and go; but these fellows camp with you and stay" </s>
<s> Then it was the guide-boards: "In a Protestant canton you couldn't get lost if you wanted to, but you never see a guide-board in a Catholic canton" </s>
<s> Next, "You never see any flower-boxes in the windows, here--never anything but now and then a cat--a torpid one; but you take a Protestant canton: windows perfectly lovely with flowers--and as for cats, there's just acres of them </s>
<s> These folks in this canton leave a road to make itself, and then fine you three francs if you 'trot' over it--as if a horse could trot over such a sarcasm of a road" </s>
<s> Next about the goiter: "THEY talk about goiter!--I haven't seen a goiter in this whole canton that I couldn't put in a hat" </s>
<s> He had growled at everything, but I judged it would puzzle him to find anything the matter with this majestic glacier </s>
<s> I intimated as much; but he was ready, and said with surly discontent: "You ought to see them in the Protestant cantons" </s>
<s> This irritated me </s>
<s> But I concealed the feeling, and asked: "What is the matter with this one" </s>
<s> "Matter </s>
<s> Why, it ain't in any kind of condition </s>
<s> They never take any care of a glacier here </s>
<s> The moraine has been spilling gravel around it, and got it all dirty" </s>
<s> "Why, man, THEY can't help that" </s>
<s> "THEY </s>
<s> You're right </s>
<s> That is, they WON'T </s>
<s> They could if they wanted to </s>
<s> You never see a speck of dirt on a Protestant glacier </s>
<s> Look at the Rhone glacier </s>
<s> It is fifteen miles long, and seven hundred feet thick </s>
<s> If this was a Protestant glacier you wouldn't see it looking like this, I can tell you" </s>
<s> "That is nonsense </s>
<s> What would they do with it" </s>
<s> "They would whitewash it </s>
<s> They always do" </s>
<s> I did not believe a word of this, but rather than have trouble I let it go; for it is a waste of breath to argue with a bigot </s>
<s> I even doubted if the Rhone glacier WAS in a Protestant canton; but I did not know, so I could not make anything by contradicting a man who would probably put me down at once with manufactured evidence </s>
<s> About nine miles from St </s>
<s> Nicholas we crossed a bridge over the raging torrent of the Visp, and came to a log strip of flimsy fencing which was pretending to secure people from tumbling over a perpendicular wall forty feet high and into the river </s>
<s> Three children were approaching; one of them, a little girl, about eight years old, was running; when pretty close to us she stumbled and fell, and her feet shot under the rail of the fence and for a moment projected over the stream </s>
<s> It gave us a sharp shock, for we thought she was gone, sure, for the ground slanted steeply, and to save herself seemed a sheer impossibility; but she managed to scramble up, and ran by us laughing </s>
<s> We went forward and examined the place and saw the long tracks which her feet had made in the dirt when they darted over the verge </s>
<s> If she had finished her trip she would have struck some big rocks in the edge of the water, and then the torrent would have snatched her downstream among the half-covered boulders and she would have been pounded to pulp in two minutes </s>
<s> We had come exceedingly near witnessing her death </s>
<s> And now Harris's contrary nature and inborn selfishness were strikingly manifested </s>
<s> He has no spirit of self-denial </s>
<s> He began straight off, and continued for an hour, to express his gratitude that the child was not destroyed </s>
<s> I never saw such a man </s>
<s> That was the kind of person he was; just so HE was gratified, he never cared anything about anybody else </s>
<s> I had noticed that trait in him, over and over again </s>
<s> Often, of course, it was mere heedlessness, mere want of reflection </s>
<s> Doubtless this may have been the case in most instances, but it was not the less hard to bar on that account--and after all, its bottom, its groundwork, was selfishness </s>
<s> There is no avoiding that conclusion </s>
<s> In the instance under consideration, I did think the indecency of running on in that way might occur to him; but no, the child was saved and he was glad, that was sufficient--he cared not a straw for MY feelings, or my loss of such a literary plum, snatched from my very mouth at the instant it was ready to drop into it </s>
<s> His selfishness was sufficient to place his own gratification in being spared suffering clear before all concern for me, his friend </s>
<s> Apparently, he did not once reflect upon the valuable details which would have fallen like a windfall to me: fishing the child out--witnessing the surprise of the family and the stir the thing would have made among the peasants--then a Swiss funeral--then the roadside monument, to be paid for by us and have our names mentioned in it </s>
<s> And we should have gone into Baedeker and been immortal </s>
<s> I was silent </s>
<s> I was too much hurt to complain </s>
<s> If he could act so, and be so heedless and so frivolous at such a time, and actually seem to glory in it, after all I had done for him, I would have cut my hand off before I would let him see that I was wounded </s>
<s> We were approaching Zermatt; consequently, we were approaching the renowned Matterhorn </s>
<s> A month before, this mountain had been only a name to us, but latterly we had been moving through a steadily thickening double row of pictures of it, done in oil, water, chromo, wood, steel, copper, crayon, and photography, and so it had at length become a shape to us--and a very distinct, decided, and familiar one, too </s>
<s> We were expecting to recognize that mountain whenever or wherever we should run across it </s>
<s> We were not deceived </s>
<s> The monarch was far away when we first saw him, but there was no such thing as mistaking him </s>
<s> He has the rare peculiarity of standing by himself; he is peculiarly steep, too, and is also most oddly shaped </s>
<s> He towers into the sky like a colossal wedge, with the upper third of its blade bent a little to the left </s>
<s> The broad base of this monster wedge is planted upon a grand glacier-paved Alpine platform whose elevation is ten thousand feet above sea-level; as the wedge itself is some five thousand feet high, it follows that its apex is about fifteen thousand feet above sea-level </s>
<s> So the whole bulk of this stately piece of rock, this sky-cleaving monolith, is above the line of eternal snow </s>
<s> Yet while all its giant neighbors have the look of being built of solid snow, from their waists up, the Matterhorn stands black and naked and forbidding, the year round, or merely powdered or streaked with white in places, for its sides are so steep that the snow cannot stay there </s>
<s> Its strange form, its august isolation, and its majestic unkinship with its own kind, make it--so to speak--the Napoleon of the mountain world </s>
<s> "Grand, gloomy, and peculiar," is a phrase which fits it as aptly as it fitted the great captain </s>
<s> Think of a monument a mile high, standing on a pedestal two miles high </s>
<s> This is what the Matterhorn is--a monument </s>
<s> Its office, henceforth, for all time, will be to keep watch and ward over the secret resting-place of the young Lord Douglas, who, in 1865, was precipitated from the summit over a precipice four thousand feet high, and never seen again </s>
<s> No man ever had such a monument as this before; the most imposing of the world's other monuments are but atoms compared to it; and they will perish, and their places will pass from memory, but this will remain </s>
<s> [The accident which cost Lord Douglas his life (see Chapter xii) also cost the lives of three other men </s>
<s> These three fell four-fifths of a mile, and their bodies were afterward found, lying side by side, upon a glacier, whence they were borne to Zermatt and buried in the churchyard </s>
<s> The remains of Lord Douglas have never been found </s>
<s> The secret of his sepulture, like that of Moses, must remain a mystery always.] A walk from St </s>
<s> Nicholas to Zermatt is a wonderful experience </s>
<s> Nature is built on a stupendous plan in that region </s>
<s> One marches continually between walls that are piled into the skies, with their upper heights broken into a confusion of sublime shapes that gleam white and cold against the background of blue; and here and there one sees a big glacier displaying its grandeurs on the top of a precipice, or a graceful cascade leaping and flashing down the green declivities </s>
<s> There is nothing tame, or cheap, or trivial--it is all magnificent </s>
<s> That short valley is a picture-gallery of a notable kind, for it contains no mediocrities; from end to end the Creator has hung it with His masterpieces </s>
<s> We made Zermatt at three in the afternoon, nine hours out from St </s>
<s> Nicholas </s>
<s> Distance, by guide-book, twelve miles; by pedometer seventy-two </s>
<s> We were in the heart and home of the mountain-climbers, now, as all visible things testified </s>
<s> The snow-peaks did not hold themselves aloof, in aristocratic reserve; they nestled close around, in a friendly, sociable way; guides, with the ropes and axes and other implements of their fearful calling slung about their persons, roosted in a long line upon a stone wall in front of the hotel, and waited for customers; sun-burnt climbers, in mountaineering costume, and followed by their guides and porters, arrived from time to time, from breakneck expeditions among the peaks and glaciers of the High Alps; male and female tourists, on mules, filed by, in a continuous procession, hotelward-bound from wild adventures which would grow in grandeur every time they were described at the English or American fireside, and at last outgrow the possible itself </s>
<s> We were not dreaming; this was not a make-believe home of the Alp-climber, created by our heated imaginations; no, for here was Mr Girdlestone himself, the famous Englishman who hunts his way to the most formidable Alpine summits without a guide </s>
<s> I was not equal to imagining a Girdlestone; it was all I could do to even realize him, while looking straight at him at short range </s>
<s> I would rather face whole Hyde Parks of artillery than the ghastly forms of death which he has faced among the peaks and precipices of the mountains </s>
<s> There is probably no pleasure equal to the pleasure of climbing a dangerous Alp; but it is a pleasure which is confined strictly to people who can find pleasure in it </s>
<s> I have not jumped to this conclusion; I have traveled to it per gravel-train, so to speak </s>
<s> I have thought the thing all out, and am quite sure I am right </s>
<s> A born climber's appetite for climbing is hard to satisfy; when it comes upon him he is like a starving man with a feast before him; he may have other business on hand, but it must wait </s>
<s> Mr Girdlestone had had his usual summer holiday in the Alps, and had spent it in his usual way, hunting for unique chances to break his neck; his vacation was over, and his luggage packed for England, but all of a sudden a hunger had come upon him to climb the tremendous Weisshorn once more, for he had heard of a new and utterly impossible route up it </s>
<s> His baggage was unpacked at once, and now he and a friend, laden with knapsacks, ice-axes, coils of rope, and canteens of milk, were just setting out </s>
<s> They would spend the night high up among the snows, somewhere, and get up at two in the morning and finish the enterprise </s>
<s> I had a strong desire to go with them, but forced it down--a feat which Mr Girdlestone, with all his fortitude, could not do </s>
<s> Even ladies catch the climbing mania, and are unable to throw it off </s>
<s> A famous climber, of that sex, had attempted the Weisshorn a few days before our arrival, and she and her guides had lost their way in a snow-storm high up among the peaks and glaciers and been forced to wander around a good while before they could find a way down </s>
<s> When this lady reached the bottom, she had been on her feet twenty-three hours </s>
<s> Our guides, hired on the Gemmi, were already at Zermatt when we reached there </s>
<s> So there was nothing to interfere with our getting up an adventure whenever we should choose the time and the object </s>
<s> I resolved to devote my first evening in Zermatt to studying up the subject of Alpine climbing, by way of preparation </s>
<s> I read several books, and here are some of the things I found out </s>
<s> One's shoes must be strong and heavy, and have pointed hobnails in them </s>
<s> The alpenstock must be of the best wood, for if it should break, loss of life might be the result </s>
<s> One should carry an ax, to cut steps in the ice with, on the great heights </s>
<s> There must be a ladder, for there are steep bits of rock which can be surmounted with this instrument--or this utensil--but could not be surmounted without it; such an obstruction has compelled the tourist to waste hours hunting another route, when a ladder would have saved him all trouble </s>
<s> One must have from one hundred and fifty to five hundred feet of strong rope, to be used in lowering the party down steep declivities which are too steep and smooth to be traversed in any other way </s>
<s> One must have a steel hook, on another rope--a very useful thing; for when one is ascending and comes to a low bluff which is yet too high for the ladder, he swings this rope aloft like a lasso, the hook catches at the top of the bluff, and then the tourist climbs the rope, hand over hand--being always particular to try and forget that if the hook gives way he will never stop falling till he arrives in some part of Switzerland where they are not expecting him </s>
<s> Another important thing--there must be a rope to tie the whole party together with, so that if one falls from a mountain or down a bottomless chasm in a glacier, the others may brace back on the rope and save him </s>
<s> One must have a silk veil, to protect his face from snow, sleet, hail and gale, and colored goggles to protect his eyes from that dangerous enemy, snow-blindness </s>
<s> Finally, there must be some porters, to carry provisions, wine and scientific instruments, and also blanket bags for the party to sleep in </s>
<s> I closed my readings with a fearful adventure which Mr Whymper once had on the Matterhorn when he was prowling around alone, five thousand feet above the town of Breil </s>
<s> He was edging his way gingerly around the corner of a precipice where the upper edge of a sharp declivity of ice-glazed snow joined it </s>
<s> This declivity swept down a couple of hundred feet, into a gully which curved around and ended at a precipice eight hundred feet high, overlooking a glacier </s>
<s> His foot slipped, and he fell </s>
<s> He says: "My knapsack brought my head down first, and I pitched into some rocks about a dozen feet below; they caught something, and tumbled me off the edge, head over heels, into the gully; the baton was dashed from my hands, and I whirled downward in a series of bounds, each longer than the last; now over ice, now into rocks, striking my head four or five times, each time with increased force </s>
<s> The last bound sent me spinning through the air in a leap of fifty or sixty feet, from one side of the gully to the other, and I struck the rocks, luckily, with the whole of my left side </s>
<s> They caught my clothes for a moment, and I fell back on to the snow with motion arrested </s>
<s> My head fortunately came the right side up, and a few frantic catches brought me to a halt, in the neck of the gully and on the verge of the precipice </s>
<s> Baton, hat, and veil skimmed by and disappeared, and the crash of the rocks--which I had started--as they fell on to the glacier, told how narrow had been the escape from utter destruction </s>
<s> As it was, I fell nearly two hundred feet in seven or eight bounds </s>
<s> Ten feet more would have taken me in one gigantic leap of eight hundred feet on to the glacier below </s>
<s> "The situation was sufficiently serious </s>
<s> The rocks could not be let go for a moment, and the blood was spurting out of more than twenty cuts </s>
<s> The most serious ones were in the head, and I vainly tried to close them with one hand, while holding on with the other </s>
<s> It was useless; the blood gushed out in blinding jets at each pulsation </s>
<s> At last, in a moment of inspiration, I kicked out a big lump of snow and struck it as plaster on my head </s>
<s> The idea was a happy one, and the flow of blood diminished </s>
<s> Then, scrambling up, I got, not a moment too soon, to a place of safety, and fainted away </s>
<s> The sun was setting when consciousness returned, and it was pitch-dark before the Great Staircase was descended; but by a combination of luck and care, the whole four thousand seven hundred feet of descent to Breil was accomplished without a slip, or once missing the way" </s>
<s> His wounds kept him abed some days </s>
<s> Then he got up and climbed that mountain again </s>
<s> That is the way with a true Alp-climber; the more fun he has, the more he wants </s>
<s> CHAPTER XXXVII [Our Imposing Column Starts Upward] After I had finished my readings, I was no longer myself; I was tranced, uplifted, intoxicated, by the almost incredible perils and adventures I had been following my authors through, and the triumphs I had been sharing with them </s>
<s> I sat silent some time, then turned to Harris and said: "My mind is made up" </s>
<s> Something in my tone struck him: and when he glanced at my eye and read what was written there, his face paled perceptibly </s>
<s> He hesitated a moment, then said: "Speak" </s>
<s> I answered, with perfect calmness: "I will ascend the Riffelberg" </s>
<s> If I had shot my poor friend he could not have fallen from his chair more suddenly </s>
<s> If I had been his father he could not have pleaded harder to get me to give up my purpose </s>
<s> But I turned a deaf ear to all he said </s>
<s> When he perceived at last that nothing could alter my determination, he ceased to urge, and for a while the deep silence was broken only by his sobs </s>
<s> I sat in marble resolution, with my eyes fixed upon vacancy, for in spirit I was already wrestling with the perils of the mountains, and my friend sat gazing at me in adoring admiration through his tears </s>
<s> At last he threw himself upon me in a loving embrace and exclaimed in broken tones: "Your Harris will never desert you </s>
<s> We will die together" </s>
<s> I cheered the noble fellow with praises, and soon his fears were forgotten and he was eager for the adventure </s>
<s> He wanted to summon the guides at once and leave at two in the morning, as he supposed the custom was; but I explained that nobody was looking at that hour; and that the start in the dark was not usually made from the village but from the first night's resting-place on the mountain side </s>
<s> I said we would leave the village at 3 or 4 P.M </s>
<s> on the morrow; meantime he could notify the guides, and also let the public know of the attempt which we proposed to make </s>
<s> I went to bed, but not to sleep </s>
<s> No man can sleep when he is about to undertake one of these Alpine exploits </s>
<s> I tossed feverishly all night long, and was glad enough when I heard the clock strike half past eleven and knew it was time to get up for dinner </s>
<s> I rose, jaded and rusty, and went to the noon meal, where I found myself the center of interest and curiosity; for the news was already abroad </s>
<s> It is not easy to eat calmly when you are a lion; but it is very pleasant, nevertheless </s>
<s> As usual, at Zermatt, when a great ascent is about to be undertaken, everybody, native and foreign, laid aside his own projects and took up a good position to observe the start </s>
<s> The expedition consisted of 198 persons, including the mules; or 205, including the cows </s>

<s> � � � RATIONS, ETC.� � � � � APPARATUS 16 Cases Hams 25 Spring Mattresses 2 Barrels Flour 2 Hair ditto 22 Barrels Whiskey Bedding for same 1 Barrel Sugar 2 Mosquito-nets 1 Keg Lemons 29 Tents 2,000� Cigars � Scientific Instruments 1 Barrel Pies 97 Ice-axes 1 Ton of Pemmican 5 Cases Dynamite 143 Pair Crutches 7 Cans Nitroglycerin 2 Barrels Arnica 22 40-foot Ladders 1 Bale of Lint 2 Miles of Rope 27 Kegs Paregoric 154 Umbrellas It was full four o'clock in the afternoon before my cavalcade was entirely ready </s>
<s> At that hour it began to move </s>
<s> In point of numbers and spectacular effect, it was the most imposing expedition that had ever marched from Zermatt </s>
<s> I commanded the chief guide to arrange the men and animals in single file, twelve feet apart, and lash them all together on a strong rope </s>
<s> He objected that the first two miles was a dead level, with plenty of room, and that the rope was never used except in very dangerous places </s>
<s> But I would not listen to that </s>
<s> My reading had taught me that many serious accidents had happened in the Alps simply from not having the people tied up soon enough; I was not going to add one to the list </s>
<s> The guide then obeyed my order </s>
<s> When the procession stood at ease, roped together, and ready to move, I never saw a finer sight </s>
<s> It was 3,122 feet long--over half a mile; every man and me was on foot, and had on his green veil and his blue goggles, and his white rag around his hat, and his coil of rope over one shoulder and under the other, and his ice-ax in his belt, and carried his alpenstock in his left hand, his umbrella (closed) in his right, and his crutches slung at his back </s>
<s> The burdens of the pack-mules and the horns of the cows were decked with the Edelweiss and the Alpine rose </s>
<s> I and my agent were the only persons mounted </s>
<s> We were in the post of danger in the extreme rear, and tied securely to five guides apiece </s>
<s> Our armor-bearers carried our ice-axes, alpenstocks, and other implements for us </s>
<s> We were mounted upon very small donkeys, as a measure of safety; in time of peril we could straighten our legs and stand up, and let the donkey walk from under </s>
<s> Still, I cannot recommend this sort of animal--at least for excursions of mere pleasure--because his ears interrupt the view </s>
<s> I and my agent possessed the regulation mountaineering costumes, but concluded to leave them behind </s>
<s> Out of respect for the great numbers of tourists of both sexes who would be assembled in front of the hotels to see us pass, and also out of respect for the many tourists whom we expected to encounter on our expedition, we decided to make the ascent in evening dress </s>
<s> We watered the caravan at the cold stream which rushes down a trough near the end of the village, and soon afterward left the haunts of civilization behind us </s>
<s> About half past five o'clock we arrived at a bridge which spans the Visp, and after throwing over a detachment to see if it was safe, the caravan crossed without accident </s>
<s> The way now led, by a gentle ascent, carpeted with fresh green grass, to the church at Winkelmatten </s>
<s> Without stopping to examine this edifice, I executed a flank movement to the right and crossed the bridge over the Findelenbach, after first testing its strength </s>
<s> Here I deployed to the right again, and presently entered an inviting stretch of meadowland which was unoccupied save by a couple of deserted huts toward the furthest extremity </s>
<s> These meadows offered an excellent camping-place </s>
<s> We pitched our tents, supped, established a proper grade, recorded the events of the day, and then went to bed </s>
<s> We rose at two in the morning and dressed by candle-light </s>
<s> It was a dismal and chilly business </s>
<s> A few stars were shining, but the general heavens were overcast, and the great shaft of the Matterhorn was draped in a cable pall of clouds </s>
<s> The chief guide advised a delay; he said he feared it was going to rain </s>
<s> We waited until nine o'clock, and then got away in tolerably clear weather </s>
<s> Our course led up some terrific steeps, densely wooded with larches and cedars, and traversed by paths which the rains had guttered and which were obstructed by loose stones </s>
<s> To add to the danger and inconvenience, we were constantly meeting returning tourists on foot and horseback, and as constantly being crowded and battered by ascending tourists who were in a hurry and wanted to get by </s>
<s> Our troubles thickened </s>
<s> About the middle of the afternoon the seventeen guides called a halt and held a consultation </s>
<s> After consulting an hour they said their first suspicion remained intact--that is to say, they believed they were lost </s>
<s> I asked if they did not KNOW it </s>
<s> No, they said, they COULDN'T absolutely know whether they were lost or not, because none of them had ever been in that part of the country before </s>
<s> They had a strong instinct that they were lost, but they had no proofs--except that they did not know where they were </s>
<s> They had met no tourists for some time, and they considered that a suspicious sign </s>
<s> Plainly we were in an ugly fix </s>
<s> The guides were naturally unwilling to go alone and seek a way out of the difficulty; so we all went together </s>
<s> For better security we moved slow and cautiously, for the forest was very dense </s>
<s> We did not move up the mountain, but around it, hoping to strike across the old trail </s>
<s> Toward nightfall, when we were about tired out, we came up against a rock as big as a cottage </s>
<s> This barrier took all the remaining spirit out of the men, and a panic of fear and despair ensued </s>
<s> They moaned and wept, and said they should never see their homes and their dear ones again </s>
<s> Then they began to upbraid me for bringing them upon this fatal expedition </s>
<s> Some even muttered threats against me </s>
<s> Clearly it was no time to show weakness </s>
<s> So I made a speech in which I said that other Alp-climbers had been in as perilous a position as this, and yet by courage and perseverance had escaped </s>
<s> I promised to stand by them, I promised to rescue them </s>
<s> I closed by saying we had plenty of provisions to maintain us for quite a siege--and did they suppose Zermatt would allow half a mile of men and mules to mysteriously disappear during any considerable time, right above their noses, and make no inquiries </s>
<s> No, Zermatt would send out searching-expeditions and we should be saved </s>
<s> This speech had a great effect </s>
<s> The men pitched the tents with some little show of cheerfulness, and we were snugly under cover when the night shut down </s>
<s> I now reaped the reward of my wisdom in providing one article which is not mentioned in any book of Alpine adventure but this </s>
<s> I refer to the paregoric </s>
<s> But for that beneficent drug, would have not one of those men slept a moment during that fearful night </s>
<s> But for that gentle persuader they must have tossed, unsoothed, the night through; for the whiskey was for me </s>
<s> Yes, they would have risen in the morning unfitted for their heavy task </s>
<s> As it was, everybody slept but my agent and me--only we and the barkeepers </s>
<s> I would not permit myself to sleep at such a time </s>
<s> I considered myself responsible for all those lives </s>
<s> I meant to be on hand and ready, in case of avalanches up there, but I did not know it then </s>
<s> We watched the weather all through that awful night, and kept an eye on the barometer, to be prepared for the least change </s>
<s> There was not the slightest change recorded by the instrument, during the whole time </s>
<s> Words cannot describe the comfort that that friendly, hopeful, steadfast thing was to me in that season of trouble </s>
<s> It was a defective barometer, and had no hand but the stationary brass pointer, but I did not know that until afterward </s>
<s> If I should be in such a situation again, I should not wish for any barometer but that one </s>
<s> All hands rose at two in the morning and took breakfast, and as soon as it was light we roped ourselves together and went at that rock </s>
<s> For some time we tried the hook-rope and other means of scaling it, but without success--that is, without perfect success </s>
<s> The hook caught once, and Harris started up it hand over hand, but the hold broke and if there had not happened to be a chaplain sitting underneath at the time, Harris would certainly have been crippled </s>
<s> As it was, it was the chaplain </s>
<s> He took to his crutches, and I ordered the hook-rope to be laid aside </s>
<s> It was too dangerous an implement where so many people are standing around </s>
<s> We were puzzled for a while; then somebody thought of the ladders </s>
<s> One of these was leaned against the rock, and the men went up it tied together in couples </s>
<s> Another ladder was sent up for use in descending </s>
<s> At the end of half an hour everybody was over, and that rock was conquered </s>
<s> We gave our first grand shout of triumph </s>
<s> But the joy was short-lived, for somebody asked how we were going to get the animals over </s>
<s> This was a serious difficulty; in fact, it was an impossibility </s>
<s> The courage of the men began to waver immediately; once more we were threatened with a panic </s>
<s> But when the danger was most imminent, we were saved in a mysterious way </s>
<s> A mule which had attracted attention from the beginning by its disposition to experiment, tried to eat a five-pound can of nitroglycerin </s>
<s> This happened right alongside the rock </s>
<s> The explosion threw us all to the ground, and covered us with dirt and debris; it frightened us extremely, too, for the crash it made was deafening, and the violence of the shock made the ground tremble </s>
<s> However, we were grateful, for the rock was gone </s>
<s> Its place was occupied by a new cellar, about thirty feet across, by fifteen feet deep </s>
<s> The explosion was heard as far as Zermatt; and an hour and a half afterward, many citizens of that town were knocked down and quite seriously injured by descending portions of mule meat, frozen solid </s>
<s> This shows, better than any estimate in figures, how high the experimenter went </s>
<s> We had nothing to do, now, but bridge the cellar and proceed on our way </s>
<s> With a cheer the men went at their work </s>
<s> I attended to the engineering, myself </s>
<s> I appointed a strong detail to cut down trees with ice-axes and trim them for piers to support the bridge </s>
<s> This was a slow business, for ice-axes are not good to cut wood with </s>
<s> I caused my piers to be firmly set up in ranks in the cellar, and upon them I laid six of my forty-foot ladders, side by side, and laid six more on top of them </s>
<s> Upon this bridge I caused a bed of boughs to be spread, and on top of the boughs a bed of earth six inches deep </s>
<s> I stretched ropes upon either side to serve as railings, and then my bridge was complete </s>
<s> A train of elephants could have crossed it in safety and comfort </s>
<s> By nightfall the caravan was on the other side and the ladders were taken up </s>
<s> Next morning we went on in good spirits for a while, though our way was slow and difficult, by reason of the steep and rocky nature of the ground and the thickness of the forest; but at last a dull despondency crept into the men's faces and it was apparent that not only they, but even the guides, were now convinced that we were lost </s>
<s> The fact that we still met no tourists was a circumstance that was but too significant </s>
<s> Another thing seemed to suggest that we were not only lost, but very badly lost; for there must surely be searching-parties on the road before this time, yet we had seen no sign of them </s>
<s> Demoralization was spreading; something must be done, and done quickly, too </s>
<s> Fortunately, I am not unfertile in expedients </s>
<s> I contrived one now which commended itself to all, for it promised well </s>
<s> I took three-quarters of a mile of rope and fastened one end of it around the waist of a guide, and told him to go find the road, while the caravan waited </s>
<s> I instructed him to guide himself back by the rope, in case of failure; in case of success, he was to give the rope a series of violent jerks, whereupon the Expedition would go to him at once </s>
<s> He departed, and in two minutes had disappeared among the trees </s>
<s> I payed out the rope myself, while everybody watched the crawling thing with eager eyes </s>
<s> The rope crept away quite slowly, at times, at other times with some briskness </s>
<s> Twice or thrice we seemed to get the signal, and a shout was just ready to break from the men's lips when they perceived it was a false alarm </s>
<s> But at last, when over half a mile of rope had slidden away, it stopped gliding and stood absolutely still--one minute--two minutes--three--while we held our breath and watched </s>
<s> Was the guide resting </s>
<s> Was he scanning the country from some high point </s>
<s> Was he inquiring of a chance mountaineer </s>
<s> Stop,--had he fainted from excess of fatigue and anxiety </s>
<s> This thought gave us a shock </s>
<s> I was in the very first act of detailing an Expedition to succor him, when the cord was assailed with a series of such frantic jerks that I could hardly keep hold of it </s>
<s> The huzza that went up, then, was good to hear </s>
<s> "Saved </s>
<s> saved" </s>
<s> was the word that rang out, all down the long rank of the caravan </s>
<s> We rose up and started at once </s>
<s> We found the route to be good enough for a while, but it began to grow difficult, by and by, and this feature steadily increased </s>
<s> When we judged we had gone half a mile, we momently expected to see the guide; but no, he was not visible anywhere; neither was he waiting, for the rope was still moving, consequently he was doing the same </s>
<s> This argued that he had not found the road, yet, but was marching to it with some peasant </s>
<s> There was nothing for us to do but plod along--and this we did </s>
<s> At the end of three hours we were still plodding </s>
<s> This was not only mysterious, but exasperating </s>
<s> And very fatiguing, too; for we had tried hard, along at first, to catch up with the guide, but had only fagged ourselves, in vain; for although he was traveling slowly he was yet able to go faster than the hampered caravan over such ground </s>
<s> At three in the afternoon we were nearly dead with exhaustion--and still the rope was slowly gliding out </s>
<s> The murmurs against the guide had been growing steadily, and at last they were become loud and savage </s>
<s> A mutiny ensued </s>
<s> The men refused to proceed </s>
<s> They declared that we had been traveling over and over the same ground all day, in a kind of circle </s>
<s> They demanded that our end of the rope be made fast to a tree, so as to halt the guide until we could overtake him and kill him </s>
<s> This was not an unreasonable requirement, so I gave the order </s>
<s> As soon as the rope was tied, the Expedition moved forward with that alacrity which the thirst for vengeance usually inspires </s>
<s> But after a tiresome march of almost half a mile, we came to a hill covered thick with a crumbly rubbish of stones, and so steep that no man of us all was now in a condition to climb it </s>
<s> Every attempt failed, and ended in crippling somebody </s>
<s> Within twenty minutes I had five men on crutches </s>
<s> Whenever a climber tried to assist himself by the rope, it yielded and let him tumble backward </s>
<s> The frequency of this result suggested an idea to me </s>
<s> I ordered the caravan to 'bout face and form in marching order; I then made the tow-rope fast to the rear mule, and gave the command: "Mark time--by the right flank--forward--march" </s>
<s> The procession began to move, to the impressive strains of a battle-chant, and I said to myself, "Now, if the rope don't break I judge THIS will fetch that guide into the camp" </s>
<s> I watched the rope gliding down the hill, and presently when I was all fixed for triumph I was confronted by a bitter disappointment; there was no guide tied to the rope, it was only a very indignant old black ram </s>
<s> The fury of the baffled Expedition exceeded all bounds </s>
<s> They even wanted to wreak their unreasoning vengeance on this innocent dumb brute </s>
<s> But I stood between them and their prey, menaced by a bristling wall of ice-axes and alpenstocks, and proclaimed that there was but one road to this murder, and it was directly over my corpse </s>
<s> Even as I spoke I saw that my doom was sealed, except a miracle supervened to divert these madmen from their fell purpose </s>
<s> I see the sickening wall of weapons now; I see that advancing host as I saw it then, I see the hate in those cruel eyes; I remember how I drooped my head upon my breast, I feel again the sudden earthquake shock in my rear, administered by the very ram I was sacrificing myself to save; I hear once more the typhoon of laughter that burst from the assaulting column as I clove it from van to rear like a Sepoy shot from a Rodman gun </s>
<s> I was saved </s>
<s> Yes, I was saved, and by the merciful instinct of ingratitude which nature had planted in the breast of that treacherous beast </s>
<s> The grace which eloquence had failed to work in those men's hearts, had been wrought by a laugh </s>
<s> The ram was set free and my life was spared </s>
<s> We lived to find out that that guide had deserted us as soon as he had placed a half-mile between himself and us </s>
<s> To avert suspicion, he had judged it best that the line should continue to move; so he caught that ram, and at the time that he was sitting on it making the rope fast to it, we were imagining that he was lying in a swoon, overcome by fatigue and distress </s>
<s> When he allowed the ram to get up it fell to plunging around, trying to rid itself of the rope, and this was the signal which we had risen up with glad shouts to obey </s>
<s> We had followed this ram round and round in a circle all day--a thing which was proven by the discovery that we had watered the Expedition seven times at one and same spring in seven hours </s>
<s> As expert a woodman as I am, I had somehow failed to notice this until my attention was called to it by a hog </s>
<s> This hog was always wallowing there, and as he was the only hog we saw, his frequent repetition, together with his unvarying similarity to himself, finally caused me to reflect that he must be the same hog, and this led me to the deduction that this must be the same spring, also--which indeed it was </s>
<s> I made a note of this curious thing, as showing in a striking manner the relative difference between glacial action and the action of the hog </s>
<s> It is now a well-established fact that glaciers move; I consider that my observations go to show, with equal conclusiveness, that a hog in a spring does not move </s>
<s> I shall be glad to receive the opinions of other observers upon this point </s>
<s> To return, for an explanatory moment, to that guide, and then I shall be done with him </s>
<s> After leaving the ram tied to the rope, he had wandered at large a while, and then happened to run across a cow </s>
<s> Judging that a cow would naturally know more than a guide, he took her by the tail, and the result justified his judgment </s>
<s> She nibbled her leisurely way downhill till it was near milking-time, then she struck for home and towed him into Zermatt </s>
<s> CHAPTER XXXVIII [I Conquer the Gorner Grat] We went into camp on that wild spot to which that ram had brought us </s>
<s> The men were greatly fatigued </s>
<s> Their conviction that we were lost was forgotten in the cheer of a good supper, and before the reaction had a chance to set in, I loaded them up with paregoric and put them to bed </s>
<s> Next morning I was considering in my mind our desperate situation and trying to think of a remedy, when Harris came to me with a Baedeker map which showed conclusively that the mountain we were on was still in Switzerland--yes, every part of it was in Switzerland </s>
<s> So we were not lost, after all </s>
<s> This was an immense relief; it lifted the weight of two such mountains from my breast </s>
<s> I immediately had the news disseminated and the map was exhibited </s>
<s> The effect was wonderful </s>
<s> As soon as the men saw with their own eyes that they knew where they were, and that it was only the summit that was lost and not themselves, they cheered up instantly and said with one accord, let the summit take care of itself </s>
<s> Our distresses being at an end, I now determined to rest the men in camp and give the scientific department of the Expedition a chance </s>
<s> First, I made a barometric observation, to get our altitude, but I could not perceive that there was any result </s>
<s> I knew, by my scientific reading, that either thermometers or barometers ought to be boiled, to make them accurate; I did not know which it was, so I boiled them both </s>
<s> There was still no result; so I examined these instruments and discovered that they possessed radical blemishes: the barometer had no hand but the brass pointer and the ball of the thermometer was stuffed with tin-foil </s>
<s> I might have boiled those things to rags, and never found out anything </s>
<s> I hunted up another barometer; it was new and perfect </s>
<s> I boiled it half an hour in a pot of bean soup which the cooks were making </s>
<s> The result was unexpected: the instrument was not affecting at all, but there was such a strong barometer taste to the soup that the head cook, who was a most conscientious person, changed its name in the bill of fare </s>
<s> The dish was so greatly liked by all, that I ordered the cook to have barometer soup every day </s>
<s> It was believed that the barometer might eventually be injured, but I did not care for that </s>
<s> I had demonstrated to my satisfaction that it could not tell how high a mountain was, therefore I had no real use for it </s>
<s> Changes in the weather I could take care of without it; I did not wish to know when the weather was going to be good, what I wanted to know was when it was going to be bad, and this I could find out from Harris's corns </s>
<s> Harris had had his corns tested and regulated at the government observatory in Heidelberg, and one could depend upon them with confidence </s>
<s> So I transferred the new barometer to the cooking department, to be used for the official mess </s>
<s> It was found that even a pretty fair article of soup could be made from the defective barometer; so I allowed that one to be transferred to the subordinate mess </s>
<s> I next boiled the thermometer, and got a most excellent result; the mercury went up to about 200 degrees Fahrenheit </s>
<s> In the opinion of the other scientists of the Expedition, this seemed to indicate that we had attained the extraordinary altitude of two hundred thousand feet above sea-level </s>
<s> Science places the line of eternal snow at about ten thousand feet above sea-level </s>
<s> There was no snow where we were, consequently it was proven that the eternal snow-line ceases somewhere above the ten-thousand-foot level and does not begin any more </s>
<s> This was an interesting fact, and one which had not been observed by any observer before </s>
<s> It was as valuable as interesting, too, since it would open up the deserted summits of the highest Alps to population and agriculture </s>
<s> It was a proud thing to be where we were, yet it caused us a pang to reflect that but for that ram we might just as well have been two hundred thousand feet higher </s>
<s> The success of my last experiment induced me to try an experiment with my photographic apparatus </s>
<s> I got it out, and boiled one of my cameras, but the thing was a failure; it made the wood swell up and burst, and I could not see that the lenses were any better than they were before </s>
<s> I now concluded to boil a guide </s>
<s> It might improve him, it could not impair his usefulness </s>
<s> But I was not allowed to proceed </s>
<s> Guides have no feeling for science, and this one would not consent to be made uncomfortable in its interest </s>
<s> In the midst of my scientific work, one of those needless accidents happened which are always occurring among the ignorant and thoughtless </s>
<s> A porter shot at a chamois and missed it and crippled the Latinist </s>
<s> This was not a serious matter to me, for a Latinist's duties are as well performed on crutches as otherwise--but the fact remained that if the Latinist had not happened to be in the way a mule would have got that load </s>
<s> That would have been quite another matter, for when it comes down to a question of value there is a palpable difference between a Latinist and a mule </s>
<s> I could not depend on having a Latinist in the right place every time; so, to make things safe, I ordered that in the future the chamois must not be hunted within limits of the camp with any other weapon than the forefinger </s>
<s> My nerves had hardly grown quiet after this affair when they got another shake-up--one which utterly unmanned me for a moment: a rumor swept suddenly through the camp that one of the barkeepers had fallen over a precipice </s>
<s> However, it turned out that it was only a chaplain </s>
<s> I had laid in an extra force of chaplains, purposely to be prepared for emergencies like this, but by some unaccountable oversight had come away rather short-handed in the matter of barkeepers </s>
<s> On the following morning we moved on, well refreshed and in good spirits </s>
<s> I remember this day with peculiar pleasure, because it saw our road restored to us </s>
<s> Yes, we found our road again, and in quite an extraordinary way </s>
<s> We had plodded along some two hours and a half, when we came up against a solid mass of rock about twenty feet high </s>
<s> I did not need to be instructed by a mule this time </s>
<s> I was already beginning to know more than any mule in the Expedition </s>
<s> I at once put in a blast of dynamite, and lifted that rock out of the way </s>
<s> But to my surprise and mortification, I found that there had been a chalet on top of it </s>
<s> I picked up such members of the family as fell in my vicinity, and subordinates of my corps collected the rest </s>
<s> None of these poor people were injured, happily, but they were much annoyed </s>
<s> I explained to the head chaleteer just how the thing happened, and that I was only searching for the road, and would certainly have given him timely notice if I had known he was up there </s>
<s> I said I had meant no harm, and hoped I had not lowered myself in his estimation by raising him a few rods in the air </s>
<s> I said many other judicious things, and finally when I offered to rebuild his chalet, and pay for the breakages, and throw in the cellar, he was mollified and satisfied </s>
<s> He hadn't any cellar at all, before; he would not have as good a view, now, as formerly, but what he had lost in view he had gained in cellar, by exact measurement </s>
<s> He said there wasn't another hole like that in the mountains--and he would have been right if the late mule had not tried to eat up the nitroglycerin </s>
<s> I put a hundred and sixteen men at work, and they rebuilt the chalet from its own debris in fifteen minutes </s>
<s> It was a good deal more picturesque than it was before, too </s>
<s> The man said we were now on the Feil-Stutz, above the Schwegmatt--information which I was glad to get, since it gave us our position to a degree of particularity which we had not been accustomed to for a day or so </s>
<s> We also learned that we were standing at the foot of the Riffelberg proper, and that the initial chapter of our work was completed </s>
<s> We had a fine view, from here, of the energetic Visp, as it makes its first plunge into the world from under a huge arch of solid ice, worn through the foot-wall of the great Gorner Glacier; and we could also see the Furggenbach, which is the outlet of the Furggen Glacier </s>
<s> The mule-road to the summit of the Riffelberg passed right in front of the chalet, a circumstance which we almost immediately noticed, because a procession of tourists was filing along it pretty much all the time </s>
<s> "Pretty much" may not be elegant English, but it is high time it was </s>
<s> There is no elegant word or phrase which means just what it means.--M.T </s>
<s> The chaleteer's business consisted in furnishing refreshments to tourists </s>
<s> My blast had interrupted this trade for a few minutes, by breaking all the bottles on the place; but I gave the man a lot of whiskey to sell for Alpine champagne, and a lot of vinegar which would answer for Rhine wine, consequently trade was soon as brisk as ever </s>
<s> Leaving the Expedition outside to rest, I quartered myself in the chalet, with Harris, proposing to correct my journals and scientific observations before continuing the ascent </s>
<s> I had hardly begun my work when a tall, slender, vigorous American youth of about twenty-three, who was on his way down the mountain, entered and came toward me with that breezy self-complacency which is the adolescent's idea of the well-bred ease of the man of the world </s>
<s> His hair was short and parted accurately in the middle, and he had all the look of an American person who would be likely to begin his signature with an initial, and spell his middle name out </s>
<s> He introduced himself, smiling a smirky smile borrowed from the courtiers of the stage, extended a fair-skinned talon, and while he gripped my hand in it he bent his body forward three times at the hips, as the stage courtier does, and said in the airiest and most condescending and patronizing way--I quite remember his exact language: "Very glad to make your acquaintance, 'm sure; very glad indeed, assure you </s>
<s> I've read all your little efforts and greatly admired them, and when I heard you were here, I .." </s>
<s> I indicated a chair, and he sat down </s>
<s> This grandee was the grandson of an American of considerable note in his day, and not wholly forgotten yet--a man who came so near being a great man that he was quite generally accounted one while he lived </s>
<s> I slowly paced the floor, pondering scientific problems, and heard this conversation: GRANDSON </s>

<s> If you would find me, you must look in the unvisited nooks and corners where others never think of going </s>

<s> Presently the Grandson rose to leave--discovered he had an appointment with some Emperor, perhaps </s>
